The ruling of khiyar in Istisna'. He said: and he [the buyer] has the option: if he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he leaves it, because he bought something he did not see, and there is no option for the artisan. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mabsut, and it is the most correct, because he [the artisan] sold what he did not see. And from Abu Hanifa that he [the artisan] also has the option, because he cannot deliver the subject matter without harm, which is cutting the leather etc. And from Abu Yusuf that there is no option for either of them. As for the artisan, due to what we mentioned; and as for the customer, because establishing the option for him causes harm to the artisan, since no one else will buy it for the same price. And it is not valid in items in which people do not customarily transact [Istisna'], like clothes, due to the lack of permissibility; and in items in which there is custom, it is only valid when it is possible to inform by description so that delivery can be made. Translation: The customer has the option: if he wishes he takes it, if he wishes he leaves it, because he bought something he did not see, and the artisan has no option. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mabsut, and it is the most correct, because he sold what he did not see. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the artisan also has the option, because it is not possible to deliver the subject matter without harm, and that harm is cutting the leather etc. And from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that there is no option for both. As for the artisan, due to the reason we mentioned; and as for the customer, because establishing the option for him causes harm to the artisan, since another person will not buy it for the same price. And in items in which people do not customarily transact, like clothes, Istisna' is not valid due to the lack of permissibility; and in items in which there is custom, it is only valid when it is possible to inform by description so that delivery can be made. Commentary: The author explains that in Istisna', when the item is made and the customer sees it, the customer has the option because the correct view is that Istisna' is a sale and the customer is the buyer, and it was established earlier that the buyer has khiyar al-ru'yat when buying unseen. According to al-Mabsut, the artisan does not have khiyar al-ru'yat because he is the seller and the seller does not have such option. From Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a narration that the artisan also has the option due to the harm he would suffer if forced to deliver; he may withdraw to avoid that harm. From Imam Abu Yusuf, there is a narration that neither has the option: the artisan because he is the seller, and the customer because granting him the option harms the artisan, as no one else would buy the item at that price, e.g., a pulpit ordered by a preacher; if the preacher does not take it, it may remain unsold. Therefore, considering the harm to the artisan, the customer is also not given the option.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the khiyar (option) in Istisna'. The relied-upon position (al-sahih) from al-Mabsut is that only the customer (mustasni') has khiyar al-ru'yat, while the artisan does not. This is because the customer buys an unseen item, while the artisan sells an unseen item. A narration from Abu Hanifa grants the artisan an option due to the harm he would suffer from cutting materials. A narration from Abu Yusuf denies the option to both parties: the artisan because he sells unseen, and the customer because giving him the option harms the artisan (the item may not be easily resold). The passage also notes that Istisna' is only valid in items where custom (ta'amul) exists and where description is possible for delivery. The weight of authority: the view from al-Mabsut (Imam Muhammad) is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyār al-ruʾyah): The option of inspection, allowing the buyer to accept or reject an item after seeing it.
بائع (bāʿiʿ): Seller; in Istisna', the artisan is the seller.
مشتری (mushtarī): Buyer; in Istisna', the customer is the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (al-sahih) in the Hanafi school, who has khiyar al-ru'yat in an Istisna' contract?
A) Only the artisan.
B) Only the customer.
C) Both the customer and the artisan.
D) Neither the customer nor the artisan.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school is that only the customer has khiyar al-ru'yat in Istisna', as stated in al-Mabsut.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Option of Inspection in Istisna' for Customer and Manufacturer
Explains khiyar al-ru'yah for mustasni' and sani' with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) in an istisna' contract and explain the tarjih (preferred view) with its rationale.

Core Idea
In istisna', only the customer has khiyar al-ru'yah; the manufacturer does not—except in two minority narrations.

This passage from al-Hidayah (via Ashraf al-Hidayah) presents the ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah in istisna'. While the relied-upon Hanafi position grants the customer the right to reject upon inspection, there are two notable intra-school differences: one from Abu Hanifa giving the manufacturer an option, and another from Abu Yusuf denying any option to both. Understanding these variants is crucial for a mufti dealing with custom manufacturing contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi relied-upon position
The customer (mustasni') has khiyar al-ru'yah; the manufacturer (sani') does not. This is the view in al-Mabsut and considered the most sound.
The basis: istisna' is a sale, the customer is buyer, seller has no khiyar.
2
Recognize the two alternative narrations
One from Abu Hanifa gives the manufacturer an option due to potential harm; another from Abu Yusuf denies option to both parties.
These are narrated as exceptions within the school.
3
Examine the proofs for each narration
Abu Hanifa's proof: the manufacturer suffers harm (e.g., cutting leather) if forced to deliver a custom item after rejection. Abu Yusuf's proof: giving the customer an option harms the manufacturer because the custom item may not sell elsewhere.
The relied-upon view counters: the seller does not have khiyar al-ru'yah by default; the harm to the manufacturer is inherent in the custom nature.
4
Analyze the tarjih reasoning
The majority of the school (including later Hanafi masters) prefer the view of no manufacturer option because it maintains contract stability and aligns with general principles of khiyar.
Al-Mabsut explicitly states this is the relied-upon position.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the relied-upon view, the customer can return the item, but the manufacturer cannot back out. Under Abu Hanifa's narration, both can rescind. Under Abu Yusuf's narration, neither can.
Fatwa generally follows the relied-upon view, but the alternative may be applied if harm is extensive.

تشریح فاضل مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ استصناع کی صورت میں بھی بن کر تیار ہو جائے اور بنوانے والا اس کو دیکھ لے تو بنوانے والے کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے اس کو لے اور جی چاہے چھوڑ دے کیونکہ استصناع صحیح قول کے مطابق بیج ہے اور بنوانے والا مشتری ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ بغیر دیکھے خریدنے کی صورت میں مشتری کو خیار رویت حاصل ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہاں بھی مشتری یعنی بنوانے والے کو خیار رویت حاصل ہوگا ۔ اور مبسوط کے بیان کے مطابق کاریگر کو خیار، ڈیت حاصل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کا ریگر بائع ہوتا ہے اور بائع کو خیار رڈبیت حاصل نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کاریگر کو خیار رویت کے تحت معاملہ ختم کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ کاریگر کو بھی اختیار حاصل ہے جی چاہے اس کام کو کرے، جی چاہے چھوڑ دے۔ اس روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کاریگر کے لیے معقود علیہ کو بغیر ضرر کے سپرد کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ موزے یا جوتے یا اور کوئی چیز بنانے کے لیے اس کو کاٹنا پڑے گا ۔ اور کسی چیز کو کاٹ کر ٹکڑے کرنا ظاہر ہے کا ریگر کا نقصان ہے۔ پس اپنے اوپر سے ضرر اور نقصان کو دور کرنے کے لیے کاریگر اگر معاملہ ترک کرنا چاہے تو ترک کر سکتا ہے حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ کاریگر اور بنوانے والے دونوں کے لیے خیار حاصل نہ ہوگا کا ریگر کے لیے تو سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ کاریگر بائع ہوتا ہے اور بائع کے واسطے خیار رویت ثابت نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کاریگر کے لئے خیار رویت حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ اور بنوانے والے کیلئے خیار اسلئے ثابت نہیں ہو گا کہ اس کو خیار دینے میں کاریگر کا نقصان ہے بایں طور کہ کاریگر نے چھڑا وغیرہ اپنا مال اس لئے کاٹ ڈالا کہ اس کو اس کا بدل ملنے کی پوری توقع تھی لیکن اگر بنوانے والے کو خیار دے دیا اور اس نے اپنے خیار کے تحت اس چیز کو نہ لیا تو اس میں کاریگر کا نقصان ہوگا کیونکہ دوسرا آدمی اس چیز کو اتنے روپیوں کے عوض نہیں لے گا بلکہ یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ وہ چیز فروخت ہی نہ ہو۔ مثلاً : واعظ نے منبر بنوایا اور پھر اپنے اختیار کے تحت اس کو نہیں لیا تو ایک عام آدمی بے ضرورت ہونے کی وجہ سے اس منبر کو نہیں خریدے گا اور اس میں صرامر کا ریگر کا نقصان ہے ۔ پس کاریگر کے نقصان کے پیش نظر بنوانے والے کو بھی اختیار نہیں دیا گیا ہے۔
Chapter of Salam. The author said: 'And if one orders the manufacture of something from that without a fixed term...' except with harm, which is cutting the leather and other things. And from Abu Yusuf that there is no option for them. As for the manufacturer, due to what we mentioned. And as for the customer, because establishing the option for him causes harm to the manufacturer, because no one else will buy it for that price. And it is not permissible in what people do not customarily deal in, like clothes, due to lack of permissibility. And in what they do deal in, it is only permissible if it is possible to inform by description so that delivery can be made. Translation: And the one who orders has an option, whether to take it or leave it, because he bought something he did not see. And the manufacturer has no option. This is mentioned in al-Mabsut. And this is the most correct, because he sold something he did not see. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the manufacturer also has an option, because it is not possible to deliver the subject matter without harm, and that harm is cutting the leather etc. And from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that neither the customer nor the manufacturer has an option. For the manufacturer, due to the reason we mentioned. For the customer, because giving him an option would cause harm to the manufacturer, because no other person will buy it for that price. And in things where people do not customarily deal, like clothes, istisna' is not permissible due to lack of permissibility. And in things where people do deal, istisna' is permissible only when it is possible to inform by description so that delivery can be made. Commentary: The author says that in the case of istisna', when the item is made and the customer sees it, the customer has an option to take or leave, because istisna' is a sale according to the correct view, and the customer is the buyer, and it has passed that the buyer has the option of inspection when buying unseen. So here also the customer has the option of inspection. According to al-Mabsut, the manufacturer has no option, because the manufacturer is the seller, and the seller does not have the option of inspection. From Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the manufacturer also has an option, as he can choose to do the work or leave it. The proof is that it is not possible for the manufacturer to deliver the subject matter without harm because he must cut the leather for shoes or other items, and cutting causes loss. So to remove harm from himself, he can leave the transaction. From Imam Abu Yusuf there is a narration that neither has an option: the manufacturer because he is a seller (no option), and the customer because giving him an option harms the manufacturer, as the manufacturer cut his material expecting payment, but if the customer exercises his option and does not take it, the manufacturer suffers loss since no one else will buy at that price, and it may not sell at all. For example, a preacher orders a pulpit and then does not take it; a common man will not buy it due to lack of need. So due to harm to the manufacturer, the customer is also not given an option.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) in the istisna' contract. The author states the relied-upon position: the customer (mustasni') has the option to accept or reject upon seeing the completed item, because he bought it unseen. The manufacturer (sani') generally has no option because he is the seller and sellers do not have this option. Then two alternative narrations are reported: from Abu Hanifa giving the manufacturer an option due to potential harm (e.g., cutting leather), and from Abu Yusuf denying any option to both parties because giving the customer an option could unfairly harm the manufacturer. The commentary explains each position with reasoning.

Key Terms
استصناع (istisna'): A contract for the manufacture of a specific item according to given specifications.
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option to rescind a sale upon seeing the item when it was purchased unseen.
مستصنع (mustasni'): The customer who places an order for manufacture.
صائن (sani'): The manufacturer or artisan who agrees to produce the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, who has the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) in an istisna' contract?
A) Both the customer and the manufacturer.
B) Only the manufacturer.
C) Only the customer.
D) Neither, because the item is custom-made.

Key Takeaway
In istisna', the customer has the right to reject upon inspection; the manufacturer does not, though minority narrations grant him an option based on harm.

Condition of Customary Dealing (Tatamul) for Istisna'
States conditions for istisna' validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the validity of istisna' according to the Hanafi school and apply them to determine whether a given item can be ordered by istisna'.

Core Idea
Istisna' requires both customary dealing and ability to describe — without market practice, the contract is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the permissibility of istisna' (manufacturing contract). The author lays down a principle: istisna' is not permissible for any item arbitrarily; rather, it is limited to those items in which people customarily engage in such transactions. Additionally, the item must be describable so that the manufacturer can produce it accordingly. This lesson will unpack this condition and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Istisna' (contract to manufacture an item). What is the ruling? It is permissible only if two conditions are met. Identify those conditions from the text.
The ruling is not absolute permissibility; it is conditional.
2
Understand the condition of tatamul
Tatamul means customary dealing or market practice. The author states that istisna' is only valid in items where people customarily order manufacture. Why is this needed? Because istisna' is sanctioned by istihsan based on 'urf, not by qiyas.
Without tatamul, the contract lacks a basis in customary practice.
3
Understand the condition of description (awsaf)
The item must be capable of being described precisely so that the manufacturer knows what to produce. This avoids gharar (uncertainty). What happens if the item cannot be described? The contract would be invalid due to excessive uncertainty.
Description is necessary for valid specification of the subject matter.
4
Apply to the example of cloth
The text gives cloth as an example where istisna' is not permissible because there is no tatamul in ordering cloth. Even if one could describe it, the contract is invalid due to the missing condition of tatamul. Consider: why might there be no custom? Because cloth is usually sold ready-made, not custom-ordered through a manufacturer contract.
The example illustrates that both conditions are necessary; one alone is insufficient.
5
Determine the scope of valid istisna' items
To know if an item is valid for istisna', one must check: (a) Is it customarily ordered by people? (b) Can it be described sufficiently? If both yes, istisna' is valid. If either is missing, the contract is not istisna'. It may be possible through other contracts like ijarah or salam.
The mufta bihi position relies on established market practice in each locale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ ضابطہ کے طور پر فرماتے ہیں کہ جن چیزوں کو سائی دے کر بنوانے میں لوگوں کا تعامل نہیں ہے۔ ان چیزوں کو سائی دے کر بنوانا یعنی استصناع جائز نہ ہو گا۔ مثلاً کپڑا بننے والے سے سائی دے کر کپڑا بنوانا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے مجوز یعنی لوگوں کا تعامل نہیں پایا جاتا اور جن چیزوں کو سائی دے کر بنوانے میں لوگوں کا تعامل پایا جاتا ہے ان میں استصناع یعنی سائی دے کر بنوانا اس وقت جائز ہوگا ۔ جبکہ اوصاف بیان کرنے سے اس شی کے بارے میں آگاہی ہو جائے تا کہ اسی کے موافق بنا کر سپر د کرے۔
The author of al-Hidayah states as a principle: In items for which there is no customary dealing (tatamul) among people for ordering manufacture, istisna' is not permissible. For example, ordering cloth from a weaver is not permissible because there is no custom of dealing (mujawwiz) in it. And in items where there is customary dealing, istisna' is permissible only when description (awsaf) can be given so that the item can be made accordingly and delivered.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage establishes a foundational condition for the validity of istisna': the contract is only valid in goods where people customarily engage in such transactions (tatamul). If there is no market practice, the contract is invalid because it lacks a basis in 'urf. The example given is cloth: people generally do not custom-order cloth, so istisna' for cloth is invalid. For valid items, the customer must specify the necessary descriptions so the manufacturer can produce exactly that.

Key Terms
تعامل (tatamul): Customary dealing or market practice among people.
مجوز (mujawwiz): That which permits; here, the customary practice that makes istisna' permissible.
اوصاف (awsaf): Descriptions; the attributes of the item that must be specified to avoid uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is istisna' for cloth (kapaṛa) not permissible?
A) Because cloth cannot be described precisely.
B) Because there is no customary dealing in ordering cloth manufacture.
C) Because cloth requires a fixed term, which is not allowed.
D) Because cloth is not a fungible good.

Key Takeaway
Istisna' is valid only when both customary dealing (tatamul) and precise description (awsaf) are present.

Effect of a Fixed Term in Istisna': Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on term in istisna'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of stipulating a term in istisna', and explain the legal reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
When a term is fixed in istisna', Abu Hanifa holds it becomes salam; the Sahibayn hold it remains istisna'.

In the Hanafi school, istisna' (manufacturing contract) is typically concluded without a fixed term. But what happens if a term is added? This passage from Al-Hidayah reveals an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa considers the contract transformed into salam, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), maintain it as istisna'. Understanding their proofs and the role of customary dealing is key to applying the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The base text states istisna' is concluded 'without a term' (bighayri ajal). This is the default for valid istisna'.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The dispute only arises when a term is set in items where customary dealing (tatamul) exists. If no customary dealing, all agree it becomes salam.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa: With a term, it becomes salam. His proof: the subject matter is a debt (dayn), salam is established by clear ijma, while istisna' relies on custom which has doubt.
Salam's ijma is stronger, so preference (al-awla) is for salam.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn: It remains istisna'. Their proof: the word istisna' is literal (haqiqah) for that contract, so it should be preserved; the term is interpreted as a request to expedite (ta'jil), not a deferment.
If no customary dealing, the istisna' is fasid, so it becomes salam by consensus.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, all salam conditions apply (advance payment, fixed term, etc.). Under Sahibayn, the contract remains istisna' with its normal flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بغیر اجل کی قید کا فائدہ
وانعما قال بغير اجل لانه لو ضرب الاجل فيما فيه تعامل يصير سلما عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما ولو ضربه فيما لا تعامل فيه يصير سلما بالاتفاق لهما ان اللفظ حقيقة للاستصناع فيحافظ على قضيته ويُحمل الاجل على التعجيل بخلاف ما لا تعامل فيه لان ذلك استصناع فاسد فيحمل على السلم الصحيح ولابي حنيفة انه دين يحتمل السلم وجواز السلم باجماع لا شبهة فيه وفى تعاملهم الاستصناع نوع شبهة فكان الحمل على السلم اولى والله اعلم
ترجمہ اور امام مھد نے فرمایا بغیر اجل کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیزوں میں میعاد لگائی جن میں لوگوں کا تعامل ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ سلم ہو جائے گی ۔ صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے اور اگر ایسی چیز میں میعاد بیان کی جن میں لوگوں کا تعامل نہیں ہے تو وہ بالا تفاق سلم ہو جائے گی ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استصناع کا لفظ اپنے حقیقی معنی میں استصناع کے واسطے ہے تو لفظ کے مقتضی پر اس کی محافظت کی جائے گی اور میعاد کو جلدی پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ برخلاف ایسی چیز کے جس کے بنوانے کا تعامل نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ استصناع فاسد ہے۔ پس اس کو صحیح سلم پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز بنوائی ہے وہ دین ہے احتمال رکھتا ہے سلم کا بھی اور سلم کا جائز ہونا ایسے اجماع سے ثابت ہے جس میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے اور لوگوں کے استصناع پر تعامل کرنے میں ایک طرح کا شبہ ہے۔ پس سلم پر محمول کرنا اولی ہے۔ واللہ تعالی اعلم
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ متن کی عبارت و ان استصنع شيئا من ذلك بغير اجل میں بغیر اجل کا فائدہ ذکر فرمار ہے ہیں۔ یعنی متن میں بغیر اجل اسلئے کہا کہ جن چیزوں کو سائی دے کر بنوانے میں لوگوں کا تعامل ہے اگر ان میں اجل اور میعاد بیان کی گئی تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ بیع سلم کہلائے گی اور اس کے جواز کے لئے سلم کی تمام شرطوں کا پایا جانا ضروری ہوگا ۔ یہی قول امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ لیکن صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ استصناع رہے گا سلم نہ ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ یہاں دو قسم ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ ایسی چیز ہو جس کے بنوانے کا لوگوں میں تعامل ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ ایسی چیز ہو جس کے بنوانے کا لوگوں میں تعامل نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر ایسی چیز بنوائی جس کے بنوانے میں لوگوں کا تعامل جاری ہے اور ایک میعاد مقرر کر دی ۔ مثلاً : یہ کہا کہ میں نے اس قدردام تجھے دیئے تا کہ مجھے اس قدر موزے اس صفت کے بنا کر دو ماہ پر دے دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ عقد سلم ہو جائے گا جبکہ دو ماہ کی مدت کا بیان جلدی کے واسطے نہ ہو۔ بلکہ مسلم فیہ ادا کرنے کی مہلت ہو۔ مگر صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ استصناع ہوگا۔ اور اگر ایسی چیز بنوانے میں میعاد مقرر کی جس کے بنوانے کا تعامل جاری نہیں ہے تو یہ عقد بالا اتفاق بیع سلم ہو جائے گا۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ اگر میعادڈ کر نہ کی گئی ہو تو وہ
The benefit of the condition 'without a term'. And he (the author) said 'without a term' because if he sets a term in that which has customary dealing, it becomes salam according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the Sahibayn. And if he sets a term in that which has no customary dealing, it becomes salam by consensus. Their (Sahibayn's) proof is that the word istisna' is a haqiqah for istisna', so its implication is preserved, and the term is interpreted as expediting (ta'jil), unlike in what has no dealing, because that istisna' is fasid, so it is interpreted as a valid salam. And for Abu Hanifa, it is a debt that can be salam, and the permissibility of salam is established by ijma without any doubt, while in their customary dealing of istisna' there is some doubt, so interpreting it as salam is preferable. And Allah knows best. Translation: The author said 'without a term' because if a term is set in items where people deal, it becomes salam according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the Sahibayn. If a term is set in items where there is no dealing, it becomes salam by consensus. The Sahibayn's proof: the word istisna' is haqiqah for istisna', so its masdaq is preserved, and the term is interpreted as expediting, unlike where there is no dealing, because that istisna' is fasid, so it is interpreted as a valid salam. Abu Hanifa's proof: the ordered item is a debt that can be salam, and the validity of salam is established by ijma without doubt, while the customary dealing of istisna' involves some doubt, so interpreting it as salam is preferable. And Allah knows best. Commentary: The author mentions the benefit of 'without a term' in the matn. In items with customary dealing, if a term is set, Abu Hanifa considers it a salam contract (so all salam conditions apply), and this is also the view of Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad. But the Sahibayn maintain it as istisna'. Two cases: if there is customary dealing and a term, Abu Hanifa says it becomes salam (if the term is for deferment, not for indication of urgency). If no customary dealing, all agree it becomes salam.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of stipulating a fixed term (ajal) in an istisna' contract. The matn says 'without a term' because if a term is included, the contract may become salam. Abu Hanifa holds that if the item is customarily dealt with (tatamul) and a term is set, the contract becomes salam, requiring all salam conditions. The Sahibayn say it remains istisna' because the word istisna' is literal for that contract, and the term is interpreted as an indication to expedite, not as a deferment. However, if there is no customary dealing, the istisna' is fasid, so by consensus it becomes a valid salam. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the subject matter is a debt (dayn) that can be salam, and salam is established by clear ijma, while istisna' is based on a weaker custom, so interpreting as salam is preferable. The commentary clarifies the practical difference.

Key Terms
اجل (ajal): A fixed term or deadline for delivery in a contract.
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for future delivery of specified fungible goods.
تعامل (tatamul): Customary dealing or common practice in a particular type of transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Istisna' with a Specified Term: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Detailed analysis of the ruling when a fixed term is stipulated in an istisna' contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a fixed term in an istisna' contract and explain the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
When a term is stipulated in an istisna' contract, the legal classification may shift to salam—Abu Hanifa's precaution ensures validity.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of specifying a fixed term (ajal) in an istisna' contract. While istisna' is a customarily valid contract, the introduction of a term raises the question whether it becomes a salam contract with stricter conditions. The positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn are presented, along with their proofs, and the practical implications for contract validity are discussed.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon rule
First, note that when a term is stipulated for items not commonly made by istisna', all Hanafi imams agree that the contract becomes salam. This establishes a baseline for the dispute.
The dispute only exists for items that are customarily manufactured via istisna'.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa rules that for commonly manufactured items, a fixed term turns the contract into salam. His proof: the subject is a debt that can be salam, and salam's permissibility is established by definitive consensus, while istisna' has some doubt (shubha) due to disagreement by scholars like Zufar and al-Shafi'i.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) maintain that the contract remains istisna'. Their proof: the word istisna' is literal for that contract, so it should be preserved; the term is interpreted as urging haste (ta'jil) rather than a credit term. For non-customary items, the istisna' is invalid, so it becomes salam by agreement.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tahrir
Abu Hanifa's response: when there is doubt (shubha) in istisna' due to lack of unanimous acceptance, and salam is established by definitive consensus, it is preferable to interpret the contract as salam to ensure validity. This is supported by the maxim: 'Salam is more certain in its permissibility.'
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) states: 'فكان الحمل على السلم اولى' (interpreting it as salam is more appropriate).
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, if a term is stipulated, the contract must fulfill all conditions of salam (e.g., full payment at the contract session). Under the Sahibayn's view, the contract remains istisna' and does not require upfront payment, but must follow customary practices.
This difference affects the validity of the contract if the salam conditions are not met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانعما قال بغير اجل لانه لو ضرب الاجل فيما فيه تعامل يصير سلما عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما ولو ضربه فيما لا تعامل فيه يصير سلما بالاتفاق لهما ان اللفظ حقيقة للاستصناع فيحافظ على قضيته ويُحمل الاجل على التعجيل بخلاف ما لا تعامل فيه لان ذلك استصناع فاسد فيحمل على السلم الصحيح ولابي حنيفة انه دين يحتمل السلم وجواز السلم باجماع لا شبهة فيه وفى تعاملهم الاستصناع نوع شبهة فكان الحمل على السلم اولى والله اعلم
And he said 'without a fixed term' because if he stipulated a term in what people commonly contract (istisna'), it becomes salam according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And if he stipulated a term in something not commonly contracted, it becomes salam by agreement. Their (the two's) proof: the word is literal for istisna', so its implication is preserved, and the term is interpreted as hastening (not a credit term). Contrary to what is not commonly contracted, because that is invalid istisna', so it is interpreted as valid salam. And for Abu Hanifa: it is a debt that can be salam, and the permissibility of salam is established by consensus without doubt, while their custom of istisna' has some doubt, so interpreting it as salam is more appropriate. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of stipulating a fixed term (ajal) in an istisna' (manufacturing) contract. The author of al-Hidayah notes that in the matn, the phrase 'without a fixed term' was used deliberately. If a term is mentioned for items commonly made by istisna', Abu Hanifa rules the contract becomes salam (forward sale), requiring all conditions of salam. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, maintaining it remains istisna'. However, if the item is not commonly made by istisna', all agree it becomes salam. The Sahibayn argue that the word 'istisna' is literal for that contract, so the term should be interpreted as urging haste, not a credit deferment. For items not commonly made, the istisna' is invalid, so the term indicates salam. Abu Hanifa's proof: the subject matter is a debt (dayn) that can be subject to salam, and salam's validity is proven by conclusive consensus, whereas istisna' has only customary practice which involves some doubt from disagreements by Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Hence, interpreting the contract as salam is preferable to preserve validity.

Key Terms
استصناع (istisna'): A contract with a manufacturer to produce a specific item according to specified description.
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance at the contract session and the goods are delivered later.
اجل (ajal): A fixed term or deferred time for delivery of the manufactured item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When a fixed term is mentioned for items commonly made by istisna'
B) When no term is mentioned
C) When the item is not commonly made by istisna'
D) Only if both parties explicitly intend salam

Key Takeaway
When a fixed term is stipulated in an istisna' contract, the dominant Hanafi view is that it converts into a salam contract, requiring all salam conditions, due to the stronger proof for salam and the doubt surrounding istisna'.

Sale of Dogs, Leopards, and Predatory Animals
Ruling on selling dogs and predatory animals with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling dogs and predatory animals, explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding biting dogs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi dalil.

Core Idea
A dog's benefit as a hunter or guard makes it property, so selling it is valid despite impurity claims.

This passage addresses a practical yet often misunderstood area of Islamic commercial law: the sale of dogs and predatory animals. While many assume dogs are entirely prohibited from sale due to their impurity and the hadith concerning the 'price of a dog,' the Hanafi school adopts a nuanced position that balances benefit with textual evidence. This lesson will unpack the Hanafi ruling, examine the intra-school disagreement involving Abu Yusuf, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the general ruling from the matn: selling dogs, leopards, and predatory animals is permissible, regardless of training.
Note that the matn says 'trained and untrained are the same'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits selling dogs entirely, citing the hadith about suht and the impurity of dogs.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i uses the hadith 'the price of a dog is suht' and the principle that a najis al-ayn object cannot be honored by sale.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis interpret the suht hadith as a discouragement (ibtida') against keeping dogs, not a prohibition of sale. They also reject that dogs are najis al-ayn; even if accepted, it only affects consumption.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow the sale of beneficial dogs (hunting, herding) while Shafi'is consider such sales invalid and the price haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز بيع الكلب والفهد والسباع المعلم وغير المعلم في ذلك سواء وعن أبي يوسف انه لا يجوز بيع الكلب العقور لانه غير منتفع به وقال الشافعى لا يجوز بيع الكلب لقوله عليه السلام ان من السحت مهر البغى وثمن الكلب ولانه نجس العين والنجاسة تشعر بهوان المحل وجواز البيع يشعر باعزازه فكان منتفيا ولنا انه عليه السلام نهى عن بيع الكلب الا كلب صيد او ماشية ولانه منتفع به حراسة واصطيادا فكان مالا فيجوز بيعه بخلاف الهوام الموذية لانه لا ينتفع بها والحديث محمول على الابتداء قلعا لهم عن الاقتناء ولا سلم اسة العين ولوسل فيحرم التناول دون البيع
He said: It is permissible to sell dogs, leopards, and predatory animals; trained and untrained are the same in this. And from Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible to sell a biting dog because it is not beneficial. And al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible to sell a dog because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed, from al-suht (illicit gain) is the dowry of a prostitute and the price of a dog.' And because it is impure in essence (najis al-ayn), and impurity indicates degradation, while permissibility of sale indicates honor, so it is negated. And for us (Hanafis): the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the sale of a dog except a hunting dog or a herd dog. And because it is beneficial for guarding and hunting, so it is property (mal), thus its sale is permissible. Unlike harmful vermin because there is no benefit in them. And the hadith is interpreted as discouragement (ibtida') to make them desist from keeping them. And we do not accept that it is impure in essence; and even if accepted, it prohibits consumption but not sale.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on selling dogs and predatory animals, contrasting with Ibn Yusuf's dissent and Imam al-Shafi'i's view. The matn states that selling dogs, leopards, and predatory animals is permissible, whether trained or not. However, Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) does not permit selling a biting (fierce) dog because it lacks beneficial purpose. Al-Shafi'i prohibits selling all dogs based on the hadith: '...the price of a dog' and because a dog is najis al-ayn (impure in essence), which implies it is worthless, whereas sale requires value. The Hanafi response: The Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically excepted hunting and herd dogs from the prohibition, indicating their sale is permissible. Dogs have benefit (guarding, hunting), so they are considered property (mal). The hadith is interpreted as a precaution to discourage keeping dogs, not an absolute prohibition of sale. As for najis al-ayn, Hanafis do not hold that dogs are essentially impure; rather, their impurity is limited to the saliva and body (mild). Even if one accepts the impurity, it only affects consumption, not sale. Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: sale of beneficial dogs is valid.

Key Terms
سحت (suht): Ill-gotten or illicit gain, specifically mentioned in hadith regarding price of dog and prostitute's dowry.
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): A substance considered impure in its very essence, such as pigs and dogs according to Shafi'i.
معلم (mu'allam): Trained, particularly for hunting or herding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling dogs and predatory animals when they provide benefit, interpreting the hadith restrictions as preventive measures rather than outright prohibitions.

The Hanafi Ruling on Selling Dogs: Permissibility Despite Shafi'i Objections
Ruling with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on dog sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sale of dogs and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments using Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Sale of dogs is permissible in Hanafi law because benefit makes them property, despite Shafi'i claims of impurity and prohibition.

The sale of dogs is a practical issue in many Muslim communities. While Imam al-Shafi'i absolutely prohibits it, the Hanafi school permits it for beneficial purposes such as hunting and guarding. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling, the intra-Hanafi difference over biting dogs, and a detailed rebuttal of the Shafi'i proofs. By studying this dispute, you will learn how different schools weigh hadith evidence and the concept of benefit (manfa'ah) in determining property status.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
Read the opening statement by Imam al-Quduri: the sale of dogs, cheetahs, and predators is permissible, whether trained or untrained. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
Note the intra-Hanafi exception: Imam Abu Yusuf prohibits a biting dog.
2
Identify the Shafi'i Proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith that the price of a dog is among unlawful earnings (suhut) and the argument that a dog is intrinsically impure (najis al-'ayn), thus cannot be honored by sale.
These proofs seem strong, but the Hanafi response challenges both.
3
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis counter with (a) the hadith exempting hunting and guard dogs, proving permissibility for beneficial dogs; (b) the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr imposing compensation for killing a dog, proving it is valuable property; (c) rational argument that benefit constitutes property (mal). They also argue that the prohibition hadith is abrogated or specific to an earlier period.
Pay attention to the use of dalalat al-nass to extend the ruling to all dogs.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis can engage in buying/selling dogs for lawful purposes; Shafi'is consider such transactions invalid and sinful.
This difference affects many modern scenarios, from hunting dogs to security dogs.

Source Text

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ کتے، چیتے اور درندوں کی بیع جائز ہے۔ اس حکم میں سدھایا (سکھایا ) ہوا اور نہ سدھایا ہوا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ کلب عقور کی بیع نا جائز ہے اسلئے کہ وہ قابل انتفاع نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ کتے کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ زانیہ کی اجرت اور کتے کی قیمت حرام ہیں۔ اور اسلئے کہ کتا نجس العین ہے اور نجاست محل کے ذلیل ہونے کی خبر دیتی ہے اور بیع کا جائز ہونا اس کے اعزاز کی خبر دیتا ہے۔ اسلئے بیع منتفی ہوگی۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور نے کتے کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے سوائے شکاری کتے یا حفاظت کے کتے کے ، اور اسلئے کہ کتے سے حفاظت اور شکار کرنے کا نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے۔ لہذاوہ مال ہوگا اور اسکی بیع جائز ہوگی۔ برخلاف موذی کیڑے مکوڑوں کے اسلئے کہ ان سے نفع نہیں اٹھایا جاتا ہے اور حدیث ابتدائے اسلام پر محمول ہے تا کہ کتے پالنے سے ان کو بالکلیہ جدا کیا جاسکے۔ اور کتے کا نجس العین ہونا تسلیم نہیں ہے اور اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حرام ہے نہ کہ اس کی بیع۔

السلام نهى عن بيع الكلب الا كلب صيد او ماشية " یعنی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کتے کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے سوائے شکاری کتے یا حفاظت کے کتے کی بیع کے۔ یعنی شکاری اور ریوڑ یا مکان کی حفاظت کے کتے کی بیع جائز ہے۔ مگر یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ دلیل ، دعوی سے خاص ہے کیونکہ دعوی تو یہ ہے کہ مطلقاً کتے کی بیع جائز ہے اور حدیث فقط کلب صید اور کلب ماشیہ کی بیع کے جواز کا فائدہ دیتی ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں حدیث بیان کرنے کا مقصد خصم یعنی امام شافعی کے مذہب کو باطل کرنا ہے کیونکہ وہ مطلقاً کتے کی بیع کے عدم جواز کا دعویٰ کرتے ہیں حالانکہ حدیث سے شکاری اور حفاظت کے کتے کی بیع کا جواز ثابت ہے اور دعوی کے اثبات یعنی مطلقا کتے کی بیع کے جواز پر ہماری طرف سے عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص کی یہ حدیث دلیل ہے انه عليه السلام قضى فى كلب قتله رجل باربعين درهما یعنی ایک آدمی نے ایک کتے کو مار ڈالا تو اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چالیس درہم کے تاوان کا فیصلہ فرمایا، اس روایت میں کتا مطلق ہے اور ہلاک کرنے پر تاوان واجب کیا گیا ہے اور تاوان واجب کرنا کتے کے متقوم یعنی قیمتی ہونے کی دلیل ہے اور مال متقوم کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے کتے کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔ لیکن اس پر یہ اشکال ہے کہ امام طحاوی نے شرح آثار میں یہ حدیث فی کلب صید کے الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر فرمائی ہے۔ اس صورت میں شکاری کتے کا متقوم ہونا ثابت ہوگا مطلقاً کتے کا متقوم ہونا ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ بہتر جواب یہ ہے کہ حديث نهى عن بيع الكلب الا كلب صيد او ماشية سے تمام کتوں کی بیع کا جواز ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ہر کتا جانوروں کے ریوڑ کی حفاظت کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے اس طور پر کہ چور اور بھیڑیے وغیر ہ کو دیکھ کر تمام کتے بھونکتے ہیں اور ان کا یہ بھونکنا ہی حفاظت کرتا ہے۔ پس لفظ ماشیة کے تحت تمام کتے داخل ہو گئے ۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ كلب صید اور کلب ماشیہ کی بیع کا جواز تو حدیث سے صراحت اور عبارت النص سے ثابت ہے اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے کتے ان کے ساتھ دلالۃ النص کے طور پر لاحق ہیں۔ اس طرح تمام کتوں کی بیع کا جائز ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری طرف سے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مطلقاً کتا قابل انتفاع ہے ان سے حفاظت کا کام بھی لیا جاتا ہے اور شکار کا کام بھی لیا جاتا ہے اور جو چیز منتفع بہ ہوتی ہے وہ مال ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مال آدمی کے علاوہ اس چیز کا نام ہے جو شرعاً آدمی کے نفع کیلئے پیدا کیا گیا ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقاً کتا مال ہے اور مال کی بیع جائز ہے۔ لہذا کتے کی بیع بھی جائز ہوگی۔ برخلاف سانپ ، بچھو وغیرہ موذی جانوروں کے کہ ان کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ حشرات الارض غیر منتفع بہا ہیں بلکہ ایک گونہ مضر اور ضرر رساں ہیں اور جو چیز نا قابل انتفاع ہو وہ مال نہیں اور جو چیز نا ہوتی اور جو چیز مال نہ ہو اسکی بیع بھی جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے حشرات الارض اور ہوام الارض کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ان من السحت مهر البغى و ثمن الكلب کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث ابتدائے اسلام پر محمول ہے، یعنی ابتدائے اسلام میں کتے کی بیع کے حرام ہونے کا حکم تھا لیکن بعد میں یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا ہے جیسا کہ حديث ان النبي رخص في ثمن كلب الصيد اس پر شاہد ہے یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے شکاری کتے کے ثمن کی اجازت دی ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ لوگ کتے پالتے تھے اور ان سے بے پناہ الفت اور محبت کرتے تھے اور ان کے ذریعہ بچوں اور غریبوں کو اذیتیں پہنچاتے تھے ۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو پالنے سے منع فرمایا تو لوگوں پر یہ بہت شاق گزرا۔ پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کی محبت و مودت کو کھ ونے کا ارادہ کیا گیا۔
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah Muqaddimah Tarnjumah. Quduri said: The sale of dogs, cheetahs, and predators is permissible. In this ruling, trained and untrained are equal. And from Imam Abu Yusuf there is a narration that the sale of a biting dog is impermissible because it is not beneficial. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: The sale of a dog is not permissible because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The earnings of a prostitute, the price of a dog, and the gain of a cupper are unlawful.' And because a dog is intrinsically impure, and impurity indicates the meanness of the locus, while the permissibility of sale indicates its honor; therefore the sale is invalid. Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of dogs except the hunting dog or the guard dog, and because benefit (protection and hunting) is derived from dogs; therefore it is property and its sale is permissible. Unlike harmful insects, because no benefit is derived from them. The hadith (prohibiting dog sale) is interpreted as abrogated to completely discourage keeping dogs. And the dog being intrinsically impure is not conceded; if conceded, its meat is unlawful, not its sale. Commentary: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: The sale of dogs, cheetahs, and predators such as lion, wolf etc. is permissible. The absolute expression of Sahib al-Quduri indicates that in this ruling, trained (mu'allam) and untrained are equal. The sign of a trained dog or predator is that when released for hunting it runs, when stopped it stops, and when it attacks prey it holds it for the owner without eating it. From Imam Abu Yusuf there is a narration that the sale of a biting dog (kalb 'aqur) is impermissible. Kalb 'aqur is a dog that does not accept training. Its impermissibility is because it is completely non-beneficial. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Absolutely, the sale of a dog is impermissible. The proof is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah... (detailed hadith texts). From these hadiths it is understood that the price of a dog is unlawful, and price is obtained through sale, so the cause (sale) is also unlawful. Second proof: the dog is intrinsically impure because its saliva is impure, and its meat is impure and unlawful. And sale of an intrinsically impure item is impermissible because impurity requires the locus to be base and low, while sale requires it to be honored. Our proof is the hadith: 'He (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of a dog except the hunting dog or the herd dog.' This shows the permissibility of selling hunting and guard dogs. Objection: the evidence is specific to the claim (general permissibility). Answer: The purpose is to refute al-Shafi'i who absolutely prohibits, while the hadith proves permissibility of some dogs. For general permissibility, we have the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr: 'He (peace be upon him) judged for a dog killed by a man to be compensated with forty dirhams.' This shows the dog is valuable property (mutaqawwim), and sale of valuable property is permissible. But there is an objection that Imam al-Tahawi recorded this hadith with 'hunting dog' wording. Better answer: The hadith 'prohibited sale of dog except hunting or herd dog' proves permissibility of all dogs because every dog has the capacity to guard, as they bark at thieves and wolves; thus the word 'mashiyah' includes all dogs. Second answer: By dalalat al-nass, other dogs are annexed to the explicitly mentioned ones. Our rational proof: Dogs are absolutely beneficial (for guarding and hunting), and beneficial things are property (mal). Therefore their sale is permissible. Unlike harmful creatures like snakes, scorpions, etc., which are not beneficial. The hadith of al-Shafi'i (on unlawful price) is interpreted as applying to the early period of Islam, then abrogated by the hadith permitting the price of a hunting dog. The wisdom was to wean people from excessive attachment to dogs.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of selling dogs, cheetahs, and predators. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi ruling as stated by Imam al-Quduri: the sale of these animals is permissible, whether trained or untrained. Then an intra-Hanafi difference is noted: Imam Abu Yusuf narrates that the sale of a biting dog (kalb 'aqur) is impermissible because it is not beneficial. The main dispute is with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds all dog sales impermissible based on two proofs: (1) the hadith of Abu Hurayrah and others that the price of a dog is among the unlawful earnings (suhut), and (2) the dog's intrinsic impurity (najis al-'ayn) which precludes honor required for a valid sale. The Hanafi response is two-fold: First, they cite a hadith that exempts hunting and guard dogs from the prohibition, implying permissibility for beneficial dogs. Second, they argue rationally that dogs provide benefit (protection, hunting), and anything beneficial is property (mal) whose sale is valid. The commentary (tashrih) further elaborates: it clarifies the sign of a trained dog, refutes objections to the Hanafi proof (e.g., that the hadith only specifies two types), and provides additional evidence from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr regarding compensation for killing a dog, which indicates the dog is valuable property. It also answers the Shafi'i hadith by claiming abrogation (naskh) or that it was specific to a time when dog ownership was prohibited to prevent harm. The passage thus upholds the Hanafi position that dogs can be sold for lawful benefit, contrary to the Shafi'i absolute prohibition.

Key Terms
کلب عقور (kalb 'aqur): A biting, untamed dog that does not accept training and is non-beneficial.
معلم / غیر معلم (mu'allam / ghayr mu'allam): Trained (for hunting or guarding) vs untrained animal; both are equally permissible in Quduri's ruling.
نجس العین (najis al-'ayn): Intrinsically impure substance; Hanafis argue that dog is not najis al-'ayn for sale purposes.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Valuable property in Islamic law; saleable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is the ruling on selling a trained hunting dog?
A) It is impermissible because all dog sales are forbidden.
B) It is permissible because the hadith exempts hunting dogs.
C) It is permissible only if the dog is also used for guarding.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the sale of dogs and other predators because they are beneficial property, contrary to the absolute prohibition held by al-Shafi'i.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Selling Dogs: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi response to Shafi'i prohibition of dog sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling dogs, identify the proofs from hadith and reason, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments and the Hanafi responses.

Core Idea
Dogs are valuable property; their sale is permissible unless for harmful animals.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of selling dogs. The Hanafis argue that dogs are beneficial property (mal mutaqawwim) and thus their sale is allowed, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that dogs are impure and their price is ill-gotten. We will examine the textual and rational proofs on both sides and see how the Hanafis rebut the Shafi'i arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the sale of dogs is permissible (jayiz) because dogs are beneficial property. Exception: harmful animals (like snakes) cannot be sold.
Note that the text uses 'جائز' (permissible) as the general ruling.
2
Identify the primary Hanafi proofs
Find the two hadith cited: (1) The Prophet forbade sale except hunting and guard dogs — this implies permissibility for those categories. (2) The Prophet judged forty dirhams compensation for a killed dog, showing it is valuable property.
Also note the rational proof: dogs are beneficial, hence property.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i position and its proofs
State the Shafi'i view: sale of dogs is prohibited absolutely. Their proofs: hadith 'the price of a dog is ill-gotten (suht)' and the claim that dogs are najis al-ayn (impure in essence).
The text also mentions Shafi'i's analogy to human excrement.
4
Examine the Hanafi responses
The Hanafis respond: (a) the suht hadith is abrogated — initially prohibited to reduce attachment, later permitted. (b) Impurity does not prevent sale; dung (gobar) is impure but sold. (c) Even if dogs were impure, only eating is haram, not selling. (d) Analogy from exception: all dogs capable of guarding are included under 'livestock dog'.
The text offers two sub-responses for the 'except' hadith: inclusion via general guarding ability and via qiyas.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Identify thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis permit buying and selling dogs; Shafi'is prohibit it entirely. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is permissibility.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles regarding abrogation and definition of property.

لوگ کتے پالتے تھے اور ان سے بے پناہ الفت اور محبت کرتے تھے اور ان کے ذریعہ بچوں اور غریبوں کو اذیتیں پہنچاتے تھے ۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو پالنے سے منع فرمایا تو لوگوں پر یہ بہت شاق گزرا۔ پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کی محبت و مودت کو لوگوں کے دلوں سے نکالنے کے لئے ان کو قتل کرنے کا امر فرمایا اور ان کی بیع سے منع فرمایا اور اگر کتے نے برتن میں منہ ڈال دیا تو اس برتن کو سات بار بلکہ آٹھ بار تک دھونے اور مانجھنے کا حکم فرمایا۔ پھر جب لوگوں کے دلوں سے ان کی محبت نکل گئی تو ان کی خرید وفروخت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا تھا۔ اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہو گیا ہے کہ ابتداء میں کتے کی خرید و فروخت ممنوع تھی پھر یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا اور کتے کی بیع کو جائز قرار دیا گیا۔
امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کتے کا نجس العین ہونا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے کیونکہ حالت اختیار میں ہبہ اور وصیت کے ذریعہ کتے کا دوسرے کو مالک کرنا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ نجس العین چیز کا مالک کرنا جائز نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کہتا نجس العین نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر کتے کا نجس العین ہونا تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حرام ہے، بیچنا حرام نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ مینگنیاں اور گو بر نجس العین ہیں۔ مگر ہمارے نزدیک ان کا بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی پاکخانہ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی جس طرح انسان کے پائخانہ کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح گو بر وغیرہ کی بیچ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوبر اور مینگنیاں لوگوں کے نزدیک بلانکیر مال منتفع بہ ہیں اور مال منتفع بہ کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے گوبر اور مینگنیوں کی بیع جائز ہے۔ رہا پاکتا نہ تو وہ بذات خود مشلع یہ نہیں ہے اسلئے اس کی بیچ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ بان اگر پائخانہ مٹی میں مل گیا تو مٹی کے تابع ہو کر اس کی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter of Salam (but text discusses dog sale)... ... it is not permissible to sell a dog except a hunting dog or a guard dog. Our proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'He forbade the sale of a dog except a hunting dog or a livestock dog.' ... There is an objection: the proof is more specific than the claim... The answer: the purpose is to refute Imam Shafi'i... Our proof for absolute permissibility is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) judged concerning a dog killed by a man, that he must pay forty dirhams.' ... This shows the dog is valuable property... The best answer is that the hadith 'forbade the sale of a dog except a hunting dog or a livestock dog' includes all dogs because every dog has the ability to guard... The second answer is that by indication of analogy (dalalat al-qiyas), other dogs are joined to them. Our rational proof is that dogs are beneficial for guarding and hunting, and whatever is beneficial is property (mal)... Harmful creatures like snakes and scorpions are not beneficial, so their sale is not allowed. The hadith of Imam Shafi'i 'from the ill-gotten is the dowry of a prostitute and the price of a dog' is abrogated... It was initially prohibited to remove people's attachment to dogs, then later permitted. As for the argument that dogs are impure (najis al-ayn), we do not accept it because giving a dog as a gift or bequest is valid, and an impure thing cannot be owned. Even if accepted, impurity makes eating it haram, not selling it. Dung and manure are impure but their sale is permissible according to us. Imam Shafi'i analogizes to human excrement, but our proof is that dung is beneficial property (mal muntafa' bihi).
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of dogs between the Hanafis and Imam Shafi'i. The text begins by stating the Hanafi position: the sale of dogs is permissible, citing the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that forbids the sale of a dog except a hunting dog or a guard dog. This exception implies permissibility for those categories. The text then raises an objection: the hadith is more specific than the claim of absolute permissibility. The answer is that the purpose of citing the hadith is to refute Imam Shafi'i who prohibits all dog sales entirely. For absolute permissibility, the Hanafis adduce another hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged that a person who kills a dog must pay forty dirhams as compensation. This shows the dog is valuable property (mal mutaqawwim), and the sale of valuable property is permissible. An objection is noted that Imam Tahawi narrated this hadith with the wording 'concerning a hunting dog,' so it only proves the value of a hunting dog, not all dogs. The text provides two responses: first, the hadith 'except a hunting dog or a livestock dog' includes all dogs because every dog can guard, and 'livestock' (mashiyah) covers them; second, by analogy (qiyas) the ruling of permissibility extends to all dogs. A rational proof follows: dogs are beneficial (muntafa' bihi) for guarding and hunting, so they are property, and the sale of property is permissible. Harmful animals like snakes and scorpions are not beneficial, hence their sale is not permissible. The text then addresses the Shafi'i proof: the hadith that 'the price of a dog is ill-gotten (suht)' is abrogated. Initially, dogs were prohibited due to excessive attachment; later, when people's attachment diminished, the prohibition was lifted. Finally, the text refutes the Shafi'i claim that dogs are impure (najis al-ayn). The Hanafis argue that impurity does not prevent sale; dung and manure are impure but their sale is permissible according to the Hanafis, unlike human excrement which is not beneficial. The text emphasizes that beneficial impurity allows sale.

Key Terms
كلب (kalb): Dog; a domesticated animal used for guarding, herding, or hunting.
مال متقوم (māl mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and permissible to benefit from in Islamic law.
سحت (suht): Ill-gotten gain; that which is forbidden and impure in earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, what is the primary evidence that a dog is considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim)?
A) The hadith that the Prophet forbade the sale of a dog except for hunting or livestock.
B) The hadith that the Prophet judged compensation of forty dirhams for a killed dog.
C) The hadith that the price of a dog is ill-gotten (suht).
D) The rational argument that dogs are impure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis permit the sale of dogs because they are beneficial property, and the prohibitory hadith is abrogated.

Ruling on Selling Wine and Pigs
Text and commentary on prohibition of selling wine and pigs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of wine and pigs and explain the proofs (Quran, hadith, and the concept of mal) that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Wine and pigs are not property (mal) for Muslims; their sale is invalid and haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the sale of wine (khamr) and pigs (khinzir). The matn from Al-Hidayah declares such sales impermissible, citing a hadith that the prohibition of drinking extends to selling and consuming the price. The commentary further grounds the ruling in Quranic verses and the principle that these items are not considered property (mal) for Muslims, making any transaction void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sale of wine and pigs. The text states it is not permissible (la yajuz), which implies haram and invalid (batil).
2
Locate the primary proof (hadith)
The author cites the hadith: 'The One who made its drinking forbidden has also forbidden its sale and consuming its price.' This shows the prohibition is explicit for wine; pig is included by analogy (qiyas) because it is also haram to consume.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its dalala is qat'i.
3
Locate the secondary proofs (Quran and mal concept)
The commentary adds Quran 5:90 (wine is rijs) and 5:3 (pig flesh forbidden). Since these are haram to use, they cannot be property (mal), and a sale without a valid subject matter (mal) is void.
The concept of mal is key: Hanafis define mal as something normally kept and beneficial. Wine and pigs have no lawful benefit for Muslims.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The ruling is derived from the combination of textual prohibition and the absence of mal status. Even if the contract has offer and acceptance, the subject matter is not legally recognized, so the contract is batil (void) and sinful.
This differs from merely makruh or haram but valid contracts.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab status
All major schools forbid the sale, but the Hanafi reliance on non-mal status leads to different applications, e.g., whether a dhimmi can sell wine. The Hanafi position is that wine is not mal for anyone under Muslim jurisdiction.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul definitions of mal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شراب اور خنزیر کی بیع کا حکم
قال ولا يجوز بيع الخمر والخنزير لقوله عليه السلام فيه ان الذي حرم شر بها حرم بيعها واكل ثمنها ولانه ليس بمال في حقنا وقد ذكرناه
ترجمہ اور شراب اور سور کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے شراب کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے اس کا پینا حرام کیا ہےاسی نے اسکا بیچنا اور اس کے ثمن کا کھانا بھی حرام کیا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ یہ ہمارے حق میں مال نہیں ہے اور ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ شراب اور سور کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ شراب حرام ہونے میں اصل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنْصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَان اور رجس، حرام اور نجس کو کہتے ہیں اور حرام چیز میں چونکہ تصرف جائز نہیں ہوتا اسلئے شراب میں بیع وغیرہ کے ذریعہ تصرف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور سور حرام ہونے میں اصل یہ آیت ہے: حُرمت عليكُمُ المَيْتَةُ وَالدَّمُ وَلَحْمُ الخِنزير
پس چونکہ سور بھی حرام ہے اور حرام چیز میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ اسلئے سور کی بیچ بھی ناجائز ہوگی۔ شراب کی بیع حرام ہونے پر صاحب ہدایہ کی پیش کردہ حدیث بھی شاہد ہے۔ عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق پوری حدیث یہ ہے
ان رجلا بنی ثقیف یعنی ابا عامر كان يهدى رسول الله كل عام رادية من خمر فاهدى اليه في العام الذى حرمت رادية كما كان يهدى فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يا ابا عامر ان الله تعالى قد حرم الخمر فلا يا
Ruling on selling wine and pigs. He said: 'And the sale of wine and pigs is not permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The One who made its drinking forbidden has also forbidden its sale and consuming its price.' And because it is not property (mal) in our right, and we have mentioned it.' Translation: The sale of wine and pig is not permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding wine: 'The One who made its drinking forbidden has also forbidden its sale and consuming its price.' And because it is not property in our right, and we have mentioned it. Explanation: The sale of wine and pig is not permissible. The original proof for wine being forbidden is Allah's saying: 'Indeed, wine, gambling, stone altars, and divining arrows are abomination (rijs) from the work of Satan.' And rijs means forbidden and impure, and because disposing of a forbidden thing is not permissible, therefore disposing of wine through sale etc. is not permissible. And the original proof for pig being forbidden is the verse: 'Forbidden to you are dead animals, blood, and the flesh of swine.' So since the pig is also forbidden, and disposing of a forbidden thing is not permissible, therefore the sale of pig is also prohibited. The hadith presented by the author of Hidayah also witnesses the prohibition of selling wine. According to the Inayah, the complete hadith is: 'A man from Thaqif, Abu Amir, used to gift the Prophet a load of wine every year. In the year wine was forbidden, he gifted as usual. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: O Abu Amir, Allah has forbidden wine, so do not...'
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on selling wine (khamr) and pigs (khinzir) with proofs. It begins with the matn: 'And the sale of wine and pigs is not permissible.' The proof is the hadith: 'Allah made wine's drinking haram, and also its sale and consuming its price.' Additionally, wine and pigs are not considered property (mal) for Muslims, as clarified earlier. The commentary expands by citing Quranic verses: for wine, Surah al-Ma'idah 5:90, which describes it as rijs (abomination), meaning forbidden and impure. Therefore, any transaction involving it is invalid. For pigs, the verse 5:3 states that the flesh of swine is forbidden. Since the thing itself is haram, one cannot sell it. The text also mentions that the hadith cited by the author of Al-Hidayah is from the narration of Abu Amir of Thaqif, who used to gift wine to the Prophet. The Prophet refused after the prohibition. This reinforces that wine has no property value for Muslims. The ruling is clear: both wine and pigs are not property (ghayr mal) in Islamic law for Muslims, so no sale contract involving them is valid. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine; any intoxicating drink made from grapes. The term is extended to all intoxicants by analogy.
خنزير (khinzir): Pig, swine; the animal whose flesh is forbidden in the Quran.
رجس (rijs): Abomination; a thing that is impure and forbidden by divine command.
مال (mal): Property; something of value that can be owned and traded. Wine and pigs are not considered property for Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, why is the sale of wine and pigs absolutely invalid?
A) Because they are impure and impurity makes sale impermissible.
B) Because they are not considered property (mal) for Muslims, so there is no valid subject matter.
C) Because the seller must be Muslim.
D) Because the hadith only forbids drinking, not selling.

Key Takeaway
The sale of wine and pigs is invalid because they are not property (mal) for Muslims; the prohibition is embedded in the very nature of the item.

Hanafi Ruling on Selling Dogs and Refutation of Imam Shafi'i
Response to Imam Shafi'i's argument against dog sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling dogs and explain the two-part response to Imam Shafi'i's argument.

Core Idea
Sale of dogs is permissible – even if impure, beneficial property can be sold.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author refutes Imam Shafi'i's prohibition of dog sales using two arguments: first, a dog is not intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn) because it can be owned through gift or bequest; second, even if it were impure, sale is still permissible as with dung and manure. This lesson traces the Hanafi legal reasoning and the cross-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on selling dogs: initially prohibited, then abrogated; now permissible (mubah).
The passage explicitly mentions abrogation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Shafi'i holds that selling dogs is impermissible because dogs are najis al-ayn.
Shafi'i's evidence: dogs are impure by essence, so sale is invalid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Shafi'i's analogical reasoning: dog is like human excrement – both impure, so sale is impermissible.
The passage states: 'Imam Shafi'i analogizes it to human excrement.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal has two parts: (1) a dog is not najis al-ayn because ownership through gift/bequest is allowed; (2) even if it were, impurity does not forbid sale – dung and manure are impure but saleable as beneficial property (mal muntafi' bih).
The key distinction: custom ('urf) determines benefit; human excrement lacks benefit, so its sale is prohibited.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis permit dog sales; Shafi'is prohibit them. This affects everyday transactions.
Mufta bihi in Hanafi school: sale of dogs is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوگوں کے دلوں سے نکالنے کے لئے ان کو قتل کرنے کا امر فرمایا اور ان کی بیع سے منع فرمایا اور اگر کتے نے برتن میں منہ ڈال دیا تو اس برتن کو سات بار بلکہ آٹھ بار تک دھونے اور مانجھنے کا حکم فرمایا۔ پھر جب لوگوں کے دلوں سے ان کی محبت نکل گئی تو ان کی خرید وفروخت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا تھا۔ اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہو گیا ہے کہ ابتداء میں کتے کی خرید و فروخت ممنوع تھی پھر یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا اور کتے کی بیع کو جائز قرار دیا گیا۔
امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کتے کا نجس العین ہونا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے کیونکہ حالت اختیار میں ہبہ اور وصیت کے ذریعہ کتے کا دوسرے کو مالک کرنا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ نجس العین چیز کا مالک کرنا جائز نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کہتا نجس العین نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر کتے کا نجس العین ہونا تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حرام ہے، بیچنا حرام نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ مینگنیاں اور گو بر نجس العین ہیں۔ مگر ہمارے نزدیک ان کا بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی پاکخانہ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی جس طرح انسان کے پائخانہ کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح گو بر وغیرہ کی بیچ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوبر اور مینگنیاں لوگوں کے نزدیک بلانکیر مال منتفع بہ ہیں اور مال منتفع بہ کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے گوبر اور مینگنیوں کی بیع جائز ہے۔ رہا پاکتا نہ تو وہ بذات خود مشلع یہ نہیں ہے اسلئے اس کی بیچ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ بان اگر پائخانہ مٹی میں مل گیا تو مٹی کے تابع ہو کر اس کی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔
To remove [dogs] from people's hearts, He commanded to kill them and prohibited their sale. And if a dog put its mouth in a vessel, He commanded to wash it seven times, even eight times. Then when love for them left people's hearts, their purchase and sale were deemed permissible. From this detail it is known that in the beginning the sale and purchase of dogs was prohibited, then this ruling was abrogated and the sale of dogs was deemed permissible. In response to Imam Shafi'i's rational proof, the author of Hidayah said: We do not accept that a dog is najis al-ayn (impure in itself), because in a state of discretion, it is permissible to transfer ownership of a dog through gift and bequest. And transferring ownership of something that is najis al-ayn is not permissible. So it is clear that a dog is not najis al-ayn. And if it is accepted that a dog is najis al-ayn, then eating it is forbidden, but selling it is not forbidden, just as dung and manure are najis al-ayn, but in our view selling them is permissible, although according to Imam Shafi'i it is not permissible. Imam Shafi'i analogizes it to human excrement: just as the sale of human excrement is not permissible, so the sale of manure etc. would not be permissible. Our proof is that dung and manure, without doubt, are beneficial property (mal muntafi' bih) in people's view, and the sale of beneficial property is permissible. Therefore, the sale of dung and manure is permissible. As for human excrement, it is not inherently beneficial, so its sale is not permissible. But if excrement mixes with soil, then by following the soil its sale becomes permissible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of selling dogs. The Hanafi position is that initially the sale of dogs was prohibited, but this ruling was abrogated, and now selling dogs is permissible. The author of Al-Hidayah refutes Imam Shafi'i's argument that dogs are najis al-ayn (impure in essence). He provides two rebuttals: First, if a dog were najis al-ayn, it could not be owned through gift or bequest, which is permissible. Second, even if it were najis al-ayn, its sale is still permissible because impurity does not prevent sale, as seen with dung and manure which are impure but saleable according to Hanafis. Imam Shafi'i analogizes dung to human excrement, but the Hanafi response distinguishes: dung and manure are beneficial property (mal muntafi' bih) in customary practice, while human excrement is not inherently beneficial. The Hanafi school relies on custom (urf) and istihsan in this matter.

Key Terms
نجس العین (najis al-ayn): Something that is impure in its essence; its impurity is intrinsic and not acquired.
مال منتفع بہ (mal muntafi' bih): Property that is beneficial and can be used lawfully; it is considered a valid subject of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why is the sale of dogs permissible even if one argues they are najis al-ayn?
A) Because dogs are not impure at all.
B) Because even impure items like dung are saleable if they are beneficial property.
C) Because the Prophet (PBUH) permitted it.
D) Because dogs are edible.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis permit selling dogs based on abrogation, rejection of intrinsic impurity, and the principle that beneficial impure items are saleable.

Prohibition of Selling Wine and Pigs
Ruling on selling wine and pigs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wine and pigs, explain the hadith proof, and apply the reasoning that these items are not property (mal) for Muslims.

Core Idea
Selling wine and pigs is haram because they are not property and their prohibition extends to sale.

In this lesson, we examine the clear ruling that selling wine and pigs is impermissible in Hanafi fiqh. The author presents a hadith from the Prophet (PBUH) that directly links the prohibition of drinking to the prohibition of selling, and also argues that these items are not considered property (mal) for Muslims. We will unpack the proofs and understand why this ruling is consistent across the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling wine and pigs. The ruling is ‘not permissible’ (la yajuz) which means haram and invalid.
This is a direct statement from the matn.
2
Locate the primary dalli (hadith)
The author cites a hadith: ‘The One who made drinking it forbidden has also forbidden its sale and the consumption of its price.’
The full story of Abu Amir from Thaqif is provided in the commentary.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah of the hadith
The hadith explicitly equates the prohibition of drinking with the prohibition of selling and using its price. It is a clear nassi that demands compliance.
The dalala is qat'i (definitive) in meaning, even though the hadith is ahad.
4
Identify the second proof: not property
Wine and pigs are not considered mal (property) in the right of Muslims. Since sale is a contract on property, selling non-property is invalid.
This is established earlier in the chapter on invalid sales.
5
Conclude and note cross-madhhab consensus
The Hanafi ruling is that selling wine and pigs is haram and the contract is batil (void). This is agreed upon by all four madhhabs.
Any difference in definition of mal does not affect this ruling.

And the sale of wine and pig is not permissible, because of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement regarding it: 'The One who made drinking it forbidden has also forbidden its sale and the consumption of its price.' And because it is not property in our right, and we have mentioned it. Explanation of the issue: The sale of wine and pig is not permissible. The basis for wine being forbidden is the saying of Allah: 'Indeed, wine, gambling, idols, and divining arrows are abomination from the work of Satan.' And 'abomination' means forbidden and impure. And since it is not permissible to dispose of a forbidden thing, therefore it will not be permissible to dispose of wine through sale etc. And the basis for pig being forbidden is this verse: 'Forbidden to you are carrion, blood, and the flesh of swine.' So since pig is also forbidden, and disposing of a forbidden thing is impermissible, therefore the sale of pig is also impermissible. The hadith presented by the author of Hidayah is also evidence for the prohibition of wine sale. According to 'Inayah, the full hadith is: A man from Thaqif (Abu Amir) used to gift the Prophet a large vessel of wine every year. In the year wine was prohibited, he brought it as usual. The Prophet said, 'O Abu Amir, Allah has prohibited wine, so we have no need of your wine.' He said, 'O Messenger of Allah, take it and sell it and suffice yourself with its price.' The Prophet said, 'O Abu Amir, the One who made drinking it forbidden has also forbidden its sale and the consumption of its price.' That is, a man from Thaqif whose kuniyyah was Abu Amir... (the story continues). In any case, this hadith proves the prohibition of wine sale. The second proof is that wine and pig are not property in the right of Muslims, as was detailed in the beginning of the chapter on invalid sales. And that which is not property, its sale is not permissible. Therefore, the sale of wine and pig is not permissible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that selling wine and pigs is not permissible. The proof is from the hadith of Abu Amir, where the Prophet (PBUH) said, 'The One who made drinking it forbidden has also forbidden its sale and the consumption of its price.' Additionally, these items are not considered property (mal) for Muslims as established in the section on invalid sales. The Quranic verses (al-Ma'idah 90 and al-Ma'idah 3) are cited to show their impurity and prohibition. The commentary expands on the hadith story, illustrating that even after prohibition, some might think sale is allowed, but the Prophet clearly prohibited it. The author also mentions a contemporary anecdote about pork to show the firmness of the prohibition.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Property that has value and is permissible to trade; wine and pigs are not considered mal for Muslims.

C) It is only prohibited to sell it to Muslims.
D) It is permissible if the seller is in need.

Key Takeaway
Selling wine and pigs is haram because the Prophet explicitly forbade it and these items are not considered property (mal) in Islamic law.
