Ruling on Mixed Gold and Silver Price
Explains ruling on mixed currency price in a sale contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the price in a sale mentions both gold and silver with or without specifying the unit, and explain the reasoning based on priority cancellation and custom.

Core Idea
When both gold and silver are mentioned, priorities cancel and the price splits equally; otherwise, custom determines the unit.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common ambiguity in sale contracts: when the buyer says 'a thousand mithqal of gold and silver,' how much of each is due? The Hanafi school uses the principles of equal attribution and cancellation of conflicting priorities to reach a fair division. We will explore the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ambiguous phrase
The act is buying a slave girl. The price is stated as 'a thousand mithqal of gold and silver'. The ambiguity arises because 'mithqal' is typically associated with gold, yet both metals are mentioned.
The word 'mithqal' is a unit of weight for gold, but the contract includes silver as well.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for the first scenario
The ruling is that the price is divided equally: 500 mithqal of gold and 500 mithqal of silver. This is because the word 'mithqal' is attributed equally to both, and there is no priority for one over the other.
This division is sahih (valid) because it removes ambiguity.
3
Analyze the objection and the Hanafi response
An objection might be that 'mithqal' is specific to gold, so the whole should be gold. The Hanafi response is that silver also has priority in common transactions, so the priorities cancel out, leaving equal attribution.
This illustrates the principle of ta'arud (conflict) leading to tasqit (fall) of both priorities.
4
Examine the second scenario without unit specification
If the buyer says 'a thousand of gold and silver' without specifying mithqal or dirham, then the customary unit for each applies: gold is measured in mithqals, silver in dirhams of weight seven.
Custom ('urf) determines the unit when the contract is ambiguous.
5
Derive the practical outcome
In the second scenario, the buyer owes 500 mithqals of gold and 500 dirhams of silver (with the dirham being 1/10 of 7 mithqals).
This ensures the contract is valid and the price is determinate.

اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری نے ایک ہزار کے عدد کو سونے اور چاندی کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے۔ پس جو وزن متعارف ہو گا اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور سونے میں وزن متعارف چونکہ مثاقیل ہیں اسلئے سونے کے مشاقیل واجب ہوں گے ۔ اور چاندی میں وزن متعارف چونکہ دراہم وزن سبعہ ہیں۔ اسلئے چاندی کے در اہم واجب ہوں گے۔ پس اس صورت میں پانچ سومثقال سونے کے اور پانچ سو درہم چاندی کے واجب ہوں گے۔
He said: Whoever buys a slave girl for a thousand mithqal of gold and silver, then they are two halves, because he attributed the mithqal to both equally. So from each one, five hundred mithqal is obligatory, due to lack of priority. And similarly, if he buys a slave girl for a thousand of gold and silver (without specifying mithqal), then gold requires mithqals, and silver requires dirhams of weight seven, because he attributed the thousand to both, so it refers to the customary weight in each one. Translation: And if someone bought a slave girl for a thousand mithqal of gold and silver, then both are obligatory as halves. Because he attributed the mithqal to both equally. So from each one, five hundred mithqal is obligatory, due to no priority. And similarly, if someone bought a slave girl for a thousand of gold and silver, then from gold, mithqals are obligatory, and from silver, dirhams of weight seven are obligatory, because he attributed the thousand to both, so it refers to the customary weight in each one. Explanation: The case is that a man bought a slave girl and said, 'I bought this slave girl for a thousand mithqal of gold and silver,' then the sale is valid, and the buyer owes five hundred mithqal of gold and five hundred mithqal of silver. If it is objected that gold mithqals have priority because mithqal is specific to gold, in that gold is weighed by mithqals but silver is not, then due to this priority the entire thousand should be gold mithqals. The answer is that just as gold has priority in this respect, so too silver has priority in another respect: in sale and the like, silver is generally used, not gold. So when each has one ground of priority, they conflict and both priorities fall. Then, due to the equal attribution of mithqal to both, half-half mithqals are obligatory: five hundred mithqal of gold and five hundred mithqal of silver. The second case: if someone bought a slave girl for a thousand of gold and silver without mentioning mithqal or dirhams, then gold requires five hundred mithqals, and silver requires five hundred dirhams, but the dirham considered is of weight seven, meaning ten dirhams equal seven mithqals. This detail has passed in Ashraf al-Hidaya vol. 3 p. 85. Its proof is that the buyer attributed the number thousand to gold and silver, so the customary weight is considered. Since the customary weight for gold is mithqals, gold mithqals are obligatory; for silver, the customary weight is dirhams of weight seven, so silver dirhams are obligatory. So in this case, five hundred mithqals of gold and five hundred dirhams of silver are obligatory.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the chapter of sales (bay') regarding the price when gold and silver are both mentioned. The author first states the matn from the Hidayah: if someone buys a slave girl for 'a thousand mithqal of gold and silver' (al-fu mithqal dhahab wa fidda), the price is split equally – five hundred mithqal of gold and five hundred mithqal of silver. The reasoning is that the word 'mithqal' is attributed to both equally, so each gets half, and there is no priority for one over the other. The commentary then addresses an objection: since 'mithqal' is commonly used for gold, shouldn't the whole be gold? The answer is that silver also has priority in general use in transactions, so the priorities cancel out. Then the second scenario: if the buyer says 'a thousand of gold and silver' without specifying mithqal or dirham, then the customary unit of weight for each applies: for gold, mithqals; for silver, dirhams of the 'weight seven' standard (10 dirhams = 7 mithqals). Thus, five hundred mithqals of gold and five hundred dirhams of silver are due. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of returning to custom ('urf) when the contract is ambiguous.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight, traditionally used for gold; equivalent to approximately 4.25 grams.
وزن سبعہ (wazn sab'ah): A specific weight standard where 10 dirhams equal 7 mithqals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

If someone says 'I bought this slave girl for a thousand mithqal of gold and silver,' how much gold and silver must he pay?
A) 1000 mithqal of gold only
B) 500 mithqal of gold and 500 mithqal of silver
C) 500 mithqal of gold and 500 dirhams of silver
D) 1000 mithqal of silver only

Key Takeaway
When the price mentions both gold and silver, if the unit is specified equally, the amount is split equally; if the unit is not specified, custom determines the unit for each metal.

Repayment of Debt with Counterfeit Coins: The Hanafi Dispute
Explains ruling when debtor pays bad coins unknowingly and they are spent/lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on discharge of debt when bad coins are spent and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Debt paid with bad coins: if the creditor unknowingly spends them, the debt is discharged according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi disagreement about the effect of paying a debt with counterfeit dirhams. The source passage presents the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf, each with their reasoning. By understanding this dispute, you will grasp the Hanafi approach to the role of quality (wasf) in debt repayment.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the situation: a debtor owes ten good dirhams, pays bad dirhams without the creditor's knowledge, and the creditor spends or loses the bad coins.
The creditor's lack of knowledge is critical — he accepts the coins thinking they are good.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that the debt is discharged (qada). Abu Yusuf rules that the creditor must return the bad dirhams and take back his good ones.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the majority and Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the creditor's right to quality (jidadah) is as protected as the principal (ayn). Since quality cannot be guaranteed (it has no value when compared with its genus), the creditor should return the bad coins and reclaim the good ones.
His reasoning emphasizes that quality is a recognized element of the debt.
4
Analyze the majority's reasoning
The majority argues that bad dirhams are of the same genus (silver) as the debt. Acceptance by the creditor satisfies the debt. The remaining right is only in quality, which cannot be compensated because quality has no independent value. Guaranteeing the principal again would impose a liability without precedent.
They treat the genus as paramount; quality is secondary and not compensable.
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the debtor owes nothing more after the creditor spends or loses the bad coins. According to Abu Yusuf, the creditor can still demand good dirhams. The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: does the debtor still owe good dirhams or not?

Source Text

قال ومن له على آخر عشرة دراهم جياد فقضاه زيوفا وهو لا يعلم فانفقها او هلكت فهو قضاء عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف يرد مثل زيوفه ويرجع بدراهمه لان حقه فى الوصف مرعى كهو في الاصل ولا يمكن رعایته بایجاب ضمان الوصف لانه لا قيمة له عند المقابلة بجنسه فوجب المصير الى ما قلنا ولهما انه من جنس حقه حتى لو تجوز به فيما لا يجوز الاستبدال جاز فيقع به الاستيفاء ولا يبقى حقه الا في الجودة ولا يمكن تداركها بايجاب ضمانها لما ذكرنا وكذا بايجاب ضمان الاصل لانه ايجاب له عليه ولا نظير له
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی کے دوسرے پر دس درہم کھرے ہوں مگر قرضدار نے قرض خواہ کو کھوٹے ادا کئے۔ درانحالیکہ قرض خواہ کو معلوم نہیں ہے پس قرض خواہ نے ان کو خرچ کر دیا یا وہ تلف ہو گئے تو یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ادا ہو گئے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ قرض خواہ دراہم زیوف واپس کرے اور دراہم جیاد لے لے۔ کیونکہ قرض خواہ کا حق وصف میں اسی طرح ملحوظ ہے جیسے اصل میں ملحوظ ہے اور اس حق کی رعایت وصف کا ضمان واجب کر کے ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بجنسہ مقابلہ کے وقت وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اسلئے اس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا جو ہم نے کہا طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دراہم زیوف بھی اس کے حق کی جنس سے ہیں ۔ حتی کہ اگر اس نے چشم پوشی کر کے کھونے درا ہم ایسے عقد میں لے لیے جس میں بدل لینا جائز نہیں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ پس اس سے حق حاصل ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اس کا حق باقی نہیں رہے گا مگر جودت ( کھرے) میں اور جودت کا تدارک اس کا ضمان واجب کر کے ممکن نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور اسی طرح اصل کا عمان واجب کر کے بھی ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل کا عضمان واجب کر نا قرض خواہ کیلئے خود اس کی ذات پر واجب کرتا ہے۔ حالانکہ شریعت میں اس کی کوئی نظیر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے دوسرے آدمی پر دس درہم کھرے قرض ہیں۔ پس قرضدار نے قرض خواہ کو دس کھوئے در ہم ادا کر دیئے اور قرض خواہ کو ان کے کھوٹے ہونے کا علم نہیں ہو سکا۔ مگر اس نے ان کو خرچ کر دیا یا وہ تلف ہو گئے تو طرفین کے نزدیک
He said: Whoever has upon another ten good dirhams, and he (the debtor) repays him with bad dirhams while he (the creditor) does not know, and he (the creditor) spends them or they are lost, then it is discharge according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He (the creditor) returns the like of his bad dirhams and takes back his dirhams. Because his right in the quality is considered just as in the principle, and it is not possible to observe it by imposing a guarantee of the quality, because it has no value when compared with its own genus. So it became necessary to resort to what we said. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is that it (the bad dirhams) is of the same genus as his right, such that if he disregards and takes it in a transaction where exchange is not permissible, it is permissible. So satisfaction occurs thereby, and his right remains only in the quality, and it is not possible to compensate it by imposing a guarantee of it, for the reason we mentioned. Similarly, by imposing a guarantee of the principal, because imposing it upon him is a liability upon himself, and there is no parallel to it. Translation: And if someone has ten good dirhams due from another, but the debtor repays the creditor with bad dirhams while the creditor is unaware, then the creditor spends them or they are lost, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is discharge. Imam Abu Yusuf said: The creditor should return the bad dirhams and take good dirhams. Because the creditor's right in the quality is considered just as in the principal, and it is not possible to observe that right by imposing a guarantee of the quality, because it has no value when compared with its own genus. So it became necessary to resort to what we said. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the bad dirhams are also of the same genus as his right, such that if he overlooks and takes them in a transaction where substitution is not permissible, it is permissible. So satisfaction occurs thereby, and his right remains only in the quality, and it is not possible to compensate it by imposing a guarantee, for the reason we mentioned. Similarly, by imposing a guarantee of the principal, because imposing it upon him (the debtor) is a liability upon himself, and there is no parallel to it. Explanation: The case is that a person has ten good dirhams due from another man. Then the debtor gives the creditor ten bad dirhams, and the creditor does not know they are bad. Then he spends them or they are lost. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is discharge.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a debt of good dirhams repaid with bad coins. The base text states the positions: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule that if the creditor unknowingly accepts bad dirhams and then spends them or they are lost, the debt is discharged (qada). Imam Abu Yusuf differs: the creditor must return the bad dirhams and can reclaim his good dirhams. The reasoning behind each position is explained. Abu Yusuf argues that the creditor's right to quality (jidadah) is as protected as the principal; since quality cannot be guaranteed because it has no independent value, the creditor should return the bad coins and take back his good ones. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that bad dirhams are of the same genus as the debt (silver coins), so if the creditor accepts them, the debt is satisfied. The right remains only in the quality, but quality cannot be compensated by a guarantee because it has no value when compared with its genus. Nor can the whole principal be guaranteed again because that would impose a liability on the debtor without precedent. The commentary then simplifies: when the creditor unknowingly spends or loses the bad coins, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad the debt is paid; Abu Yusuf says the creditor must return the likes of the bad coins and can then demand good ones. This issue highlights the Hanafi principle of 'consideration of quality' and the concept of 'jins' (genus) in debt repayment.

Key Terms
زيوف (ziyuf): Counterfeit or bad quality coins, as opposed to جياد (good/standard coins).
جودت (judat): Quality or goodness (of coins), i.e. being جياد (good).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a debtor gives bad dirhams to a creditor who unknowingly spends them, what is the ruling?
A) The creditor must return the bad dirhams and demand good ones
B) The debt is discharged
C) The debtor must pay double the amount
D) The creditor can demand both good dirhams and the value of the bad ones

Key Takeaway
In debt repayment, if the creditor unknowingly accepts and spends bad coins of the same genus, the debt is discharged; quality is not compensable.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Repayment with Defective Coins: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on debt discharge with defective coins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on debt discharge with defective coins, state the proofs of each side, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Defective coins of the same genus discharge the debt; quality cannot be independently compensated.

When a debtor pays defective coins of the same genus, does the debt discharge? A famous intra-Hanafi dispute arises: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes, Abu Yusuf says no. The disagreement hinges on whether the attribute of quality can be independently claimed. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the key elements: a debt of ten good dirhams (jiyad) is paid with defective ones (ziyuf); the creditor unknowingly spends or loses them.
The creditor's ignorance is crucial; knowledge would change the ruling.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the debt is discharged (qada'). Abu Yusuf holds the creditor must return the defective coins and take good ones.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in outcome.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes quality to quantity: just as deficient quantity can be claimed, deficient quality should be claimable. But since quality cannot be independently valued when compared with its genus, the only remedy is to reverse the transaction.
The illa in Abu Yusuf's qiyas: the right to attribute is like the right to essence.
4
Examine the Tarfayn's proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that defective coins are of the same genus (dirhams). Evidence: in salam, accepting defective coins knowingly is valid, showing same genus. Therefore the essence of the debt is fulfilled; the remaining quality right cannot be compensated because quality has no value, and imposing a guarantee on the essence would create a self-debt with no precedent.
The argument uses istihsan or qiyas khafi: the salam analogy establishes same genus.
5
Determine the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the debt is discharged. This is the view recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) uphold this view.

باب السلم
ASHRAF AL-HIDAYA VOL. 9
قال ومن له على آخر عشرة دراهم جياد فقضاه زيوفا وهو لا يعلم فانفقها او هلكت فهو قضاء عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف يرد مثل زيوفه ويرجع بدراهمه لان حقه فى الوصف مرعى كهو في الاصل ولا يمكن رعایته بایجاب ضمان الوصف لانه لا قيمة له عند المقابلة بجنسه فوجب المصير الى ما قلنا ولهما انه من جنس حقه حتى لو تجوز به فيما لا يجوز الاستبدال جاز فيقع به الاستيفاء ولا يبقى حقه الا في الجودة ولا يمكن تداركها بايجاب ضمانها لما ذكرنا وكذا بايجاب ضمان الاصل لانه ايجاب له عليه ولا نظير له
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی کے دوسرے پر دس درہم کھرے ہوں مگر قرضدار نے قرض خواہ کو کھوٹے ادا کئے۔ درانحالیکہ قرض خواہ کو معلوم نہیں ہے پس قرض خواہ نے ان کو خرچ کر دیا یا وہ تلف ہو گئے تو یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ادا ہو گئے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ قرض خواہ دراہم زیوف واپس کرے اور دراہم جیاد لے لے۔ کیونکہ قرض خواہ کا حق وصف میں اسی طرح ملحوظ ہے جیسے اصل میں ملحوظ ہے اور اس حق کی رعایت وصف کا ضمان واجب کر کے ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بجنسہ مقابلہ کے وقت وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اسلئے اس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا جو ہم نے کہا طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دراہم زیوف بھی اس کے حق کی جنس سے ہیں ۔ حتی کہ اگر اس نے چشم پوشی کر کے کھونے درا ہم ایسے عقد میں لے لیے جس میں بدل لینا جائز نہیں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ پس اس سے حق حاصل ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اس کا حق باقی نہیں رہے گا مگر جودت ( کھرے) میں اور جودت کا تدارک اس کا ضمان واجب کر کے ممکن نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور اسی طرح اصل کا عمان واجب کر کے بھی ممکن نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل کا عضمان واجب کر نا قرض خواہ کیلئے خود اس کی ذات پر واجب کرتا ہے۔ حالانکہ شریعت میں اس کی کوئی نظیر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے دوسرے آدمی پر دس درہم کھرے قرض ہیں۔ پس قرضدار نے قرض خواہ کو دس کھوئے در ہم ادا کر دیئے اور قرض خواہ کو ان کے کھوٹے ہونے کا علم نہیں ہو سکا۔ مگر اس نے ان کو خرچ کر دیا یا وہ تلف ہو گئے تو طرفین کے نزدیک
قرضدار کا قرضہ ادا ہو چکا ہے اس پر قرض خواہ کا کوئی حق باقی نہیں رہا۔ لیکن امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ صورت میں قرض خواہ دس در ہم کھوٹے جو خرچ کر چکا یا تلف ہو گئے ان کے مثل قرضدار کو واپس کرے اور اس سے دس درہم کھرے لے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرض خواہ کا حق جودت اور کھرا ہونے کے اعتبار سے وصف میں اسی طرح محوظ ہے جیسے مقدار کے اعتبار سے اصل میں ملحوظ ہے چنانچہ قرض خواہ کا حق اگر مقدار کے اعتبار سے کم ہو گیا مثلا دس درہم کے بجائے آٹھ نکلے تو قرض خواہ کو اپنے حق کی مقدار کے بقدر قرضدار سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے یعنی مزید دو درہم کے مطالبہ کا حق حاصل ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر قرضخواہ کا حق کیفیت کے اعتبار سے کم ہوا مثلاً جید کے بجائے زیوف نکلے تو بھی قرض خواہ کو قرضدار سے صفت جودت کے سلسلے میں رجوع کرنے کا حق حاصل ہو گا لیکن قرضدار پر تنہا صفت جودت کا ضمان واجب کرنا تو ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ شی جب اپنی جنس سے مقابل ہو تو وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی ۔ مثلاً ایک کھرے درہم کا ایک کھوٹے درہم سے اگر تبادلہ کیا گیا تو جائز ہے لیکن اگر ایک کھرے درہم کا دو کھونے درہم سے تبادلہ کیا گیا اور یہ کہا گیا کہ ایک درہم، ایک درہم کے عوض اور ایک کھوٹا درہم ، کھرے درہم کی صفت کھرے اور جودت کے عوض ہے تو یہ ربوا ہو گا اور نا جائز ہوگا اور رہو اس وقت لازم آتا ہے جبکہ علت رہوا پائے جانے کے بعد ایک عوض کم اور ایک عوض زائد ہو پس معلوم ہوا کہ شریعت اسلام نے دوکھوٹے دراہم کو ایک گھر سے درہم سے زائد شمار کیا ہے اور ایک کھوئے درہم کو کھرے درہم کی صفت جودت کی قیمت شمار نہیں کیا ہے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ منہ مقابلہ کے وقت وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور جب وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی تو قرضدار پر تنہا وصف جودت کا ضمان واجب کرنا بھی ممکن نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جس چیز کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور جب تنہا وصف جودت کا ضمان واجب کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے تو قرض خواہ کے وصف جودت کے حق کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے وہی صورت اختیار کی جائے گی جس کو امام ابو یوسف نے ذکر کیا ہے یعنی قرض خواہ در اہم زیوف کے مثل قرضدار کو واپس دے کر اس سے دراہم جیاد لے لے گا۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ در اہم زیوف بھی قرض خواہ کے حق کی جنس سے ہیں یعنی در اہم زیوف بھی دراہم ہیں اور قرض خواہ کا حق بھی دراہم ہی سے متعلق تھا اور دراہم زیوف کے قرض خواہ کے حق کی جنس سے ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد سلم میں رب السلم نے اگر دراہم جیاد کی جگہ درا ہم زیوف دے دیئے اور دونوں جدا ہو گئے پھر مسلم الیہ کو معلوم ہوا کہ در اہم کھوئے ہیں مگر مسلم الیہ نے چشم پوشی کر کے اپنا نقصان گوارا کیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ پس اگر در اہم زیوف مسلم الیہ کے حق کی جنس یعنی دراہم جیاد کی جنس نہ ہوتے تو یہ راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کے عوض دوسری چیز کا لینا ہوتا حالانکہ عقد سلم میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کا استبدال جائز نہیں ہے۔ پس مسلم الیہ کا دراہم مسلم میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کا استبدال جائز نہیں ہے۔ پس مسلم الیہ نے دراہم جیاد کی جگہ درا ہم زیوں لے کر چشم پوشی کر کے اپنا نقصان گوارا کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ عقد صرف میں عوضین پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ان کے بدلے میں کسی دوسری چیز کا لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ دراہم زیوف، دراہم جیاد کی جنس سے ہیں یعنی در اہم زیوف بھی در اہم ہیں تو قرض خواہ نے دراہم زیوف لے کر اپنا حق وصول کر لیا ہے۔ ہاں ! اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ قرض خواہ کا حق صفت جودت کھرے ہونے میں ) باقی رہ گیا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ قرض خواہ نے دراہم زیوف کی صورت میں اصل در اہم اور نفس در اہم وصول کر لیئے مگر وصف جودت کا منمان واجب کر کے قرض خواہ کے اس نقصان کا تدارک کیا جائے۔ دوم یہ کہ اصل در اہم کا ضمان واجب کر کے
Chapter of Salam. He said: And whoever has upon another ten good dirhams, and he paid him with defective [dirhams] while he did not know, then he spent them or they perished, then it is a discharge according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: He returns the like of his defective [dirhams] and takes his dirhams [good ones], because his right in the attribute is observed just as it is in the essence, and it is not possible to observe it by imposing a guarantee of the attribute because it has no value when compared with its genus, so it is necessary to resort to what we said. And for them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] is that they are from the genus of his right, such that if he overlooks in a transaction where substitution is not allowed, it is permissible, so the right is fulfilled and no right remains except in quality, and it cannot be compensated by imposing a guarantee of it for what we mentioned, and likewise by imposing a guarantee of the essence because it imposes upon him and there is no precedent for it. Translation: And if someone has ten good dirhams upon another, but the debtor paid the creditor with defective ones while the creditor does not know, and the creditor spent them or they perished, then according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] it is a discharge. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: The creditor should return the defective dirhams and take good dirhams. Because the creditor's right in the attribute is observed just as in the essence, and it is not possible to observe it by imposing a guarantee of the attribute because when compared with its genus, the attribute has no value. Therefore, recourse is to what we said. The proof of the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] is that the defective dirhams are from the genus of his right. Even if he overlooks and takes defective dirhams in a transaction where substitution is not allowed, it is permissible. Thus, the right is fulfilled and no right remains except in quality, and the quality cannot be compensated by imposing a guarantee of it due to the reason we mentioned, and likewise by imposing a guarantee of the essence because it imposes upon him and there is no precedent for it in Shariah. Explanation of the issue: There is a person who owes another ten good dirhams. The debtor paid him ten defective dirhams, and the creditor did not know they were defective. Then he spent them or they perished. According to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], the debt is discharged and no right remains for the creditor. But according to Abu Yusuf, the creditor must return the like of the defective dirhams to the debtor and take from him ten good dirhams. Abu Yusuf's proof: The creditor's right in the attribute of goodness is observed just as in the quantity. If the quantity is less, he can claim the deficiency. Similarly, if the quality is defective, he can claim the quality. But imposing a guarantee solely on the attribute is impossible because when something is compared with its genus, the attribute has no value. For example, exchanging one good dirham for one defective dirham is permissible, but exchanging one good dirham for two defective dirhams with the second being compensation for the quality would be riba, showing that two defective dirhams are considered more than one good dirham, and the quality has no independent value. So since the attribute has no value, its guarantee cannot be imposed. Therefore, the only way to observe the right to quality is the method mentioned by Abu Yusuf: the creditor returns the defective dirhams and takes good ones. The proof of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: Defective dirhams are from the genus of the creditor's right. Evidence: In a salam contract, if the buyer pays defective dirhams instead of good ones and they separate, then the seller overlooks and accepts, it is valid. If defective dirhams were not of the same genus as good ones, this would be a substitution before taking possession, which is invalid. This shows they are of the same genus. Thus, the creditor received dirhams and his right is fulfilled except for the quality. The quality cannot be compensated by guarantee because it has no value, and imposing a guarantee on the essence would be imposing a liability on the creditor himself, which has no precedent.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the discharge of a debt when a debtor pays with defective coins (ziyuf) instead of good ones (jiyad), and the creditor unknowingly spends them or they are lost. The ruling is initially stated: according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the debt is discharged (qada'). Abu Yusuf, however, holds that the creditor must return the defective coins and recover good ones from the debtor. The commentary then explains the reasoning of each side.

Abu Yusuf's argument: The creditor's right includes both the quantity (the number of dirhams) and the quality (goodness). Just as a deficiency in quantity can be claimed (e.g., if only eight dirhams are paid, the creditor can demand two more), a deficiency in quality should also be claimable. However, imposing a guarantee solely on the attribute of quality is impossible because when the same genus of item is exchanged, the attribute has no independent monetary value. For example, exchanging one good dirham for one defective dirham is permissible (both are dirhams, so it's not riba), but exchanging one good dirham for two defective dirhams with the intention that the second defective dirham is compensation for the quality would be riba, as the defective dirhams are considered excess. Thus, quality cannot be separately compensated. Therefore, the only remedy is to return the defective coins and take good ones, restoring both the quantity and quality.

The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (called 'the two' or 'tarfayn'): Defective dirhams are of the same genus as good dirhams (both are dirhams). Evidence: In a salam contract, if the buyer pays defective dirhams instead of good ones and the seller accepts after knowing, it is valid. If they were different in genus, this would be a substitution of capital before possession, which is invalid. So the creditor effectively received dirhams, fulfilling the essence of the debt. The only remaining right is the quality of being good, but that cannot be compensated by imposing a guarantee because quality has no value. Moreover, imposing a guarantee on the essence (the dirham itself) would mean the creditor owes a debt to himself, which is legally baseless. Therefore, the debt is fully discharged, and the payment is valid.

The passage underscores a central principle in Hanafi fiqh: when a payment is made with items of the same genus, the debt is discharged even if the quality is inferior, provided the creditor accepts it (even implicitly by spending or loss). The difference revolves around whether the attribute can be independently claimed. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as indicated by the commentary's conclusion (the creditor has no further right).

Key Terms
زُيُوف (ziyuf): Defective or counterfeit dirhams; coins of inferior quality or less silver content.
جِيَاد (jiyad): Good, pure, or high-quality dirhams; the standard quality for repayment.
قَضَاء (qada'): Discharge or fulfillment of a debt; payment that releases the debtor from obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what happens when a debtor pays defective dirhams to a creditor who unknowingly spends them?
A) The debt is not discharged; the creditor must return the defective dirhams.
B) The debt is discharged; the creditor cannot claim compensation.
C) The creditor may claim the difference in quality as compensation.
D) The debtor must pay additional dirhams to cover the quality deficiency.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the genus matches, payment with inferior quality discharges the debt; quality alone cannot be independently compensated.

Ruling when defective dirhams are given in salam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on defective currency in salam debt repayment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding defective dirhams in salam and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In genus exchanges, attribute has no independent value; thus, receiving defective dirhams discharges the debt.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his disciple Abu Yusuf on whether a salam seller who accepted bad dirhams can later demand good ones. The ruling hinges on a key principle of usul al-fiqh: when a thing is exchanged for its own genus, the attribute (like quality) carries no legal weight. Let's explore how this principle resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
A salam contract requires payment of 10 good dirhams. The buyer pays 10 defective (bad) dirhams. The seller accepts them, then later discovers they are defective. Does the seller have any further claim against the buyer?
The dispute is about the effect of accepting defective dirhams when the debt was for good ones.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its core reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the seller's debt is fully discharged because the defective dirhams are of the same genus (dirhams) as what was owed. The attribute of quality (joodah) has no independent value in same-genus exchanges, as demonstrated by the riba prohibition: exchanging one good dirham for two bad ones is riba because the extra bad dirham would be for the attribute, which is invalid.
The key principle: attribute has no value when the thing is exchanged for its own genus.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and its reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the seller's right to quality is preserved just like quantity. If the quantity is deficient (e.g., 8 instead of 10), the seller can claim more; similarly, if quality is deficient, the seller should be able to return the bad dirhams and demand good ones.
Abu Yusuf draws an analogy between quantity and quality.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and the tarjih
The text refutes Abu Yusuf by showing that compensating for the attribute alone is legally and rationally impossible. Legally, attribute has no value in genus exchanges; rationally, attribute cannot be separated from the substance. Compensating by making the debtor liable for the bad dirhams would require the creditor to be liable for his own benefit—an unprecedented concept. Therefore, the debt is discharged. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The tarjih (preference) is based on stronger dalil and rejection of legal impossibility.

Topic of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume — Your debtor's debt has been paid, no right remains for the creditor. But Imam Abu Yusuf's school is that in the mentioned case, the creditor should return to the debtor the equivalent of ten bad dirhams which he spent or were lost, and take ten good dirhams from him. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that the creditor's right with respect to the attribute of quality and goodness is preserved just as it is preserved in the substance with respect to quantity. So if the creditor's right diminished in quantity, e.g. eight instead of ten, he can claim the deficiency; similarly if diminished in quality, e.g. bad instead of good, he can claim the quality attribute. But making the debtor liable solely for the attribute of quality is not possible because when a thing is exchanged for its own genus, the attribute has no value. For example, exchanging one good dirham for one bad dirham is permissible, but exchanging one good dirham for two bad dirhams saying 'one dirham for one dirham and one bad dirham for the attribute of goodness' would be riba, forbidden. So it is established that attribute has no value at exchange. When attribute has no value, making the debtor liable for it alone is impossible. Therefore, to observe the creditor's right to quality, the same course as mentioned by Imam Abu Yusuf is adopted: the creditor returns similar bad dirhams to the debtor and takes good dirhams from him. The opponent's argument is that bad dirhams are of the same genus as the creditor's right; they are dirhams. Proof: In a salam contract, if the buyer gives bad dirhams instead of good and they separate, then the seller discovers they are bad but overlooks it, it is valid. If bad dirhams were not of the same genus as good dirhams, it would be taking another thing before taking possession of the capital, which is not permissible in salam. So the seller's acceptance of bad dirhams with knowledge is valid. Thus, bad dirhams are of the same genus; the creditor received his right in substance. However, the right to the attribute of goodness remains. The conclusion is that the creditor received the essence of dirhams in the form of bad dirhams, but the loss of quality must be compensated either by making the debtor liable for the attribute or by making the debtor liable for the substance. But both are impossible. The first is impossible legally because attribute has no value in genus exchange, and rationally because attribute cannot be separated. The second is impossible because making the debtor liable for the substance would require that the creditor be made liable for the bad dirhams he took, for the creditor's own benefit, which has no precedent in sharia. Therefore, when the creditor took the bad dirhams, his debt is discharged, and he has no right to claim anything more from the debtor.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the salam contract where the buyer (rabb al-salam) pays with defective (bad) dirhams instead of good ones. The central issue is whether the seller (muslam ilayh) who accepted such payment can later demand good dirhams from the buyer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the seller's debt is fully discharged because the defective dirhams are still dirhams and thus of the same genus as what was owed. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the seller's right includes the attribute of goodness (joodah), and since the received dirhams lack that attribute, the seller can return them and demand good ones. The text first presents Abu Yusuf's argument that the right to quality is preserved like quantity, but then explains that making the debtor liable solely for the attribute is impossible because in exchanges of the same genus, an attribute has no independent value (as seen in the riba example). It then presents the opponents' (i.e., Abu Hanifa's) argument that bad dirhams are of the same genus, proven by the permissibility of the seller accepting them after discovery. The text concludes that since neither compensating for the attribute alone nor for the substance is possible (the latter would require the creditor to guarantee the bad dirhams for his own benefit, which is unprecedented), the debt is discharged. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the Hidayah is Abu Hanifa's view, as the text states after refuting the alternatives. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
جودت (joodah): Attribute of goodness or high quality of dirhams.
زیوف (zuyaaf/zuyoof): Bad or counterfeit dirhams, lacking the quality of good dirhams.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guaranty; here, making the debtor liable to compensate for the deficiency.
ربوا (riba): Usury or interest; prohibited increase in exchange of same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, if the buyer pays with defective dirhams and the seller accepts them, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The seller can return the defective dirhams and demand good ones.
B) The seller's debt is discharged and he has no further claim.
C) The seller must accept good dirhams plus compensation for the defect.
D) The contract is void because of riba.

Key Takeaway
In same-genus exchanges, the attribute of quality has no independent value; thus, receiving defective goods of the same genus discharges the debt.

Debt Discharge with Defective Dirhams
Conclusion: debt discharged when defective dirhams accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a creditor accepts defective dirhams and explain why no further compensation is due.

Core Idea
Accepting defective dirhams voluntarily clears the debt; quality compensation is impossible.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a debtor repays a loan with defective dirhams, and the creditor accepts them. The question is whether the creditor can later demand compensation for the quality deficiency. The Hanafi ruling, rooted in both legal principle and rational reasoning, concludes that the debt is fully discharged upon acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two impossible scenarios
The author considers two possible ways the creditor might seek redress: (1) compensation solely for the quality defect, and (2) replacement of the defective coins with good ones. Both are deemed impossible.
These are the only logical options; if both fail, the debt stands discharged.
2
Understand the legal impossibility of quality compensation
The author states that when a thing is compared with its own genus, quality has no independent value. Therefore, the Shari'ah does not impose a guarantee solely for quality.
This is based on the principle that in same-genus exchanges, only quantity and genus matter; quality is not a separate compensable attribute.
3
Understand the rational impossibility of separating quality
Quality is inseparable from the substance of the dirhams. One cannot isolate the 'goodness' from the coins to value it separately.
Hence, even if the law allowed, it is rationally impossible to quantify and compensate for quality alone.
4
Understand the impossibility of replacing the defective coins
If the creditor were to return the defective coins and demand good ones, the guarantee would benefit the creditor himself, which has no precedent in Shari'ah. Guarantee always benefits someone other than the one on whom it is imposed.
Thus, this second scenario is also legally impossible.
5
Conclude the debt discharge
Since both avenues for compensation are impossible, the only conclusion is that the debt is fully discharged when the creditor accepts the defective dirhams.
The creditor's voluntary acceptance indicates satisfaction; no further claim is permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف ابدا یہ جلد نم تدارک کیا جائے مگر یہ دونوں صورتیں ناممکن ہیں۔ پہلی صورت تو شرعاً بھی ناممکن ہے اور عقلا بھی ناممکن ہے۔ شرعا تو اسلئے ناممکن ہے کہ پہلے گذر چکا ہے کہ جب کسی شی کا مقابلہ اس کی جنس کے ساتھ کیا جائے تو وصف کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی اور جس کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو شرعاً اس کا ضمان بھی واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے تنہا وصف جودت کا قرضدار پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور عقلاً اسلئے ناممکن ہے کہ وصف جودت کو اصل در اہم سے جدا کرنا ناممکن ہے۔ پس جب وصف جودت کو اصل دراہم سے جدا کرنا ناممکن ہے تو تنہا وصف جودت کا ضمان واجب کرنا بھی ناممکن ہے اور دوسری صورت اسلئے ناممکن ہے کہ اصل در اہم کے ضمان واجب کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قرضخواہ جو دراہم زیوف لے کر خرچ کر چکا یا وہ تلف ہوئے تو ان درا ہم زیوف کا ضمان قرض خواہ پر واجب کیا جائے تا کہ قرضدار، قرض خواہ کو دراہم جیا د واپس کرے۔ پس اس صورت میں دراہم زیوف کا عمان قرض خواہ پر اسلئے واجب کیا جائے گا تا کہ اس کو دراہم جیاد حاصل ہوں تو گویا قرضخواہ پر ضمان واجب کیا گیا خود اسی کے فائدے کیلئے حالانکہ شریعت میں اس کی کوئی نظیر نہیں ہے کہ جس پر ضمان واجب کیا جائے اسی کا فائدہ ہو بلکہ ضمان ایک پر واجب کیا جاتا ہے اور فائدہ دوسرے کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب اصل دراہم کا ضمان واجب کرنے میں قرض خواہ کے فائدہ کیلئے قرض خواہ پر ہی منعمان واجب کرنالازم آتا ہے اور اس کی شریعت میں کوئی نظیر نہیں ہے تو یہ صورت بھی ناممکن ہے اور جب منمان وصف اور ضمان اصل دونوں نا ممکن ہیں تو یہی کہا جائے گا کہ قرض خواہ نے جب دراہم زیوف لے لئے تو اس کا قرضہ ادا ہو گیا۔ اب اس کو قرضدار سے کسی مزید چیز کے مطالبکا حق نہیں ہے۔
Ashraf says: This volume number should be compensated, but both scenarios are impossible. The first scenario is impossible both legally (shar'an) and rationally ('aqlan). Legally it is impossible because it has passed earlier that when something is compared with its own genus, the quality has no value; and what has no value, its guarantee is not obligatory legally. Therefore, the guarantee of the quality of goodness alone is not obligatory upon the debtor. Rationally it is impossible because separating the quality of goodness from the original dirhams is impossible. So when separating the quality of goodness from the original dirhams is impossible, then making the guarantee of the quality of goodness alone obligatory is also impossible. The second scenario is impossible because making the guarantee of the original dirhams obligatory means that the creditor, having taken the defective dirhams and spent them or they being lost, the guarantee of those defective dirhams is imposed on the creditor so that the debtor returns good dirhams to the creditor. Thus in this case, the guarantee of the defective dirhams is made obligatory on the creditor so that he may obtain good dirhams, meaning the guarantee is imposed on the creditor for his own benefit, whereas there is no precedent in the Shari'ah that the one on whom guarantee is imposed should benefit from it; rather guarantee is imposed on one and the benefit goes to another. So when making the guarantee of the original dirhams obligatory necessitates imposing the guarantee on the creditor for his own benefit, and there is no precedent for this in the Shari'ah, then this scenario is also impossible. And when both the guarantee of quality and the guarantee of the original are impossible, then it will be said that when the creditor took the defective dirhams, his debt was discharged. Now he has no right to demand anything more from the debtor.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the discharge of a debt when a creditor accepts defective dirhams. The author, commenting on a prior discussion, explains why two possible recourse scenarios are impossible both legally and rationally. The first scenario is to seek compensation solely for the quality deficiency; this fails because in debt repayment of the same genus, quality is not valued as a separate entity, and rationally one cannot isolate the quality from the coins. The second scenario is to impose a guarantee on the original defective coins so that the debtor returns better ones; this fails because it would require the guarantee to benefit the very person upon whom it is imposed, which has no precedent in Shari'ah. Consequently, once the creditor voluntarily accepts defective dirhams, the debt is fully cleared, and no further claim is permissible. This ruling aligns with the Hanafi principle that once a creditor accepts payment in any form, the debt is considered satisfied.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Financial guarantee or compensation; in this context, the obligation to replace defective coins with good ones.
قرض (qard): Loan; a contract where one party gives ownership of fungible goods to another with the obligation to return similar goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a creditor willingly accepts defective dirhams in repayment of a debt, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The debtor must replace them with good ones.
B) The creditor can claim compensation for the defect.
C) The debt is considered discharged with no further claim.
D) The contract is void and the loan continues.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, once a creditor voluntarily accepts defective dirhams in repayment of a loan, the debt is fully discharged, and no separate compensation for quality is owed.

Ownership of Birds and Eggs in Someone's Land
Ruling with proof on ownership of birds and game on land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who owns birds, eggs, and game found on someone's land and apply the condition of landowner preparation.

Core Idea
Ownerless game on unprepared land belongs to the first catcher, not the landowner.

This lesson addresses a common practical question in Hanafi fiqh: if a bird nests or a deer takes shelter on your land, do you automatically own the offspring or the animal? The Hanafi answer is nuanced and depends on whether the land was prepared for that purpose. The core ruling is supported by the hadith 'al-saydu li-man akhadhahu' (game belongs to the one who takes it).

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
From the matn: if a bird hatches chicks, lays eggs, or a deer makes a lair on someone's land without preparation, the catcher owns them, not the landowner.
2
Identify the proofs
Two proofs: (a) these items are mubah (ownerless) so the first taker owns by ihraz; (b) they are considered sayd (game) and the hadith 'al-saydu li-man akhadhahu' applies. Eggs are included because they are the origin of game, as shown by the jaza for breaking them in ihram.
The hadith has zanni thubut but qati dalala.
3
Analyze the exception
If the landowner prepared his land to attract birds or game, then he becomes the owner by virtue of his preparation. The text analogizes to a net spread for hunting vs. drying.
Preparation is key: spreading a net for catching vs. drying.
4
Apply analogies
Examples: game entering a house when the owner knows and secures it; scattered sugar falling into clothes that are gathered. These illustrate when the landowner's intent and action establish ownership.
5
Distinguish honey
Honey is different: it is considered a produce of the land, so it belongs to the landowner regardless of preparation, like trees and soil deposits.
This is an exception based on custom (urf) and istihsan.

Source Text

پرندے نے ایک آدمی کی زمین میں بچے نکالے وہ اسی کے ہوں گے جس نے ان کو پکڑا
قال إذا أفرخ طير فى ارض رجل فهو لمن اخذه وكذا اذا باض فيها وكذا اذا تكنس فيها ظبى لانه مباح سبقت يده اليه ولانه صيد وان كان يؤخذ بغير حيلة والصيد لمن اخذه وكذا البيض لانه اصل الصيد ولهذا يجب الجزاء على المحرم بكسره اوشيه وصاحب الأرض لم يعد ارضه لذلك فصار كنصب شبكة للجفاف وكما اذا دخل الصيد داره او وقع ما نثر من السكر او الدراهم في ثيابه لم يكن له مالم يكفه او كان مستعداً له بخلاف ما اذا عسل النحل في ارضه لانه عُدَّ من انزاله فيملكه تبعا لارضه كالشجر النابت فيه والتراب المجتمع في ارضه بجريان الماء
ترجمہ اگر کسی آدمی کی زمین میں پرندے نے بچے نکالے تو وہ اسی کے ہوں گے جس نے ان کو پکڑا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر کسی زمین میں انڈے دیئے اور اسی طرح اگر اس زمیں میں ہرن نے گھر بنایا کیونکہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مباح ہے جس کا ہاتھ اس کی طرف پہلے پہنچا اور اسلئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک شکار ہے اگر چہ وہ بغیر تدبیر اور حیلہ کے پکڑا گیا اور شکار اسی کا ہوتا ہے جس نے اس کو پکڑا ہو اور یہی حکم انڈوں کا ہے کیونکہ انڈے شکار کی اصل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے محرم پر انڈا توڑنے یا بھوننے سے جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے اور زمین کے مالک نے اپنی زمین کو اس کام کیلئے تیار نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس یہ سوکھانے کے واسطے جال پھیلانے کے مانند ہو گیا ہے جیسا کہ کسی گھر میں کوئی شکار داخل ہو گیا یا وہ شکر یا در اہم جن کو بکھیر ا گیا ہے وہ اس کے کپڑے میں گر گئے تو یہ اس کا مالک نہ ہو گا جب تک کہ اس کو نہ رو کے یا کپڑا اس مقصد کیلئے پھیلایا ہو، برخلاف اس کے جب اس کی زمین میں شہد کی مکھیوں نے شہد جمع کیا ہو کیونکہ شہد زمین کی حاصلات سے شمار ہوتا ہے تو اپنی زمیں کے تابع بنا کر اس کا بھی مالک ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے وہ درخت جو اسکی زمین میں اگا ہو اور جیسے وہ منی جو پانی کے بہاؤ

سے اس کی زمین میں جمع ہو گئی ہو ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگرکسی کی زمین میں کسی پرندے نے بچے نکالے یا کسی پرندے نے انڈے دیئے یا ہرن نے کسی کی زمین میں اپنے رہنے کا ٹھکانا بنا لیا اور زمین کے مالک نے اس زمین کو اس مقصد کیلئے مہیا نہ کیا ہو تو زمین کا بالک مذکورہ چیزوں کا مالک نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ جو پہلے پکڑے گا وہی ان چیزوں کا مالک ہو جائیگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ چیزیں مباح ہیں ان کا کوئی مالک نہیں ہے۔ پس جس کا ہاتھ پکڑنے کیلئے ان کی طرف پہلے بڑھ جائے گا وہی ان کا مالک ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ کہے پرندے کا بچہ اور ہرن شکار ہیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول الصيد لمن اخذہ کی وجہ سے شکار اسی کا ہوتا ہے جو اس کو پکڑ لے اگر چہ بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑا ہو یعنی بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑنا اس کو شکار ہونے سے خارج نہیں کرتا جیسے کسی کی زمین میں ایک شکار کا پاؤں ٹوٹ گیا تو یہ شکار پکڑنے والے کا ہوگا نہ کہ زمین کے مالک کا اور رہا انڈ تو اس کا حکم بھی شکار کا حکم ہے کیونکہ انڈا اگر چہ بذات خود شکار نہیں ہے لیکن شکار کی اصل اور جڑ ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر حاجی نے حالت احرام میں انڈا توڑ دیا ہو یا اس کو بھون لیا ہو تو اس پر اسی طرح جرمانہ واجب ہوتا ہے جیسے شکار کرنے والے پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ انڈا بھی شکار کے حکم میں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت و صاحب الارض لم يعد ارضه لذالك اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کرتی ہے کہ اگر صاحب الارض نے اپنی زمین کو اس مقصد کیلئے تیار کر رکھا ہے کہ پرندے اس میں بچے دیا کریں گے یا پرندے انڈے دیا کریں گے یا ہرن اس میں رہا کرے تو اس صورت میں مذکورہ چیزوں کا مالک پکڑنے والا نہ ہوگا بلکہ زمین کا مالک ان چیزوں کا مالک ہوگا ۔ اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے ایک آدمی نے اپنا جال خشک کرنے کیلئے پھیلایا ۔ اتفاق سے اس میں کوئی جانور پھنس گیا تو جو شخص اس کو پہلے پکڑ لے گا وہی اس کا مالک ہوگا اور اگر جال کے مالک نے اپنا جال خشک کرنے کیلئے نہ پھیلایا ہو بلکہ شکار کے واسطے پھیلایا ہو تو جو جانور اس میں پھنسے گا اس کا مالک پکڑنے والا نہ ہو گا بلکہ جال کا مالک اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اس کی دوسری مثال یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی کے گھر میں شکار کا جانور داخل ہوا اور مالک مکان کو اس کا علم نہ ہو سکا مگر اس نے دروازہ بند کر دیا تو یہ جانور مکان کے مالک کا نہ ہوگا بلکہ جو بھی پہلے پکڑے گا اس کا ہو گا۔ اور اگر جانور مکان میں داخل ہوا اور مکان کے مالک کو اس کا علم بھی ہو گیا پھر اس نے دروازہ اور روشندان بند کیا تو یہ جانور مالک مکان کا ہوگا تیسری مثال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے شیرینی یعنی چھوہارے یا درہم بکھیرے اور کسی آدمی کے کپڑے میں گر گئے ۔ پس اگر اس نے اپنا کپڑا اس واسطے نہ پھیلایا ہو اور نہ گرنے کے بعد کپڑے کو سمیٹنا ہو تو وہ اس کا مالک نہ ہو گا ۔ ہاں اگر اس نے اپنا کپڑا اسی مقصد کیلئے پھیلایا ہے یا کپڑا اس مقصد کیلئے نہیں پھیلایا تھا مگر چھوہارے یا دور ہم گرنے کے بعد کپڑا سمیٹ لیا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں یہی کپڑے والا مالک ہوگا۔ دوسرے کو اس میں سے لینا حلال نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر زمین، چڑیوں کے انڈوں، بچوں اور ہرن وغیرہ کیلئے مہیا نہ کی گئی ہو تو زمین کا مالک ان کا مالک نہ ہوگا بلکہ جو پہلے پکڑے گا وہی مالک قرار پائے گا اور اگر زمین ان کے لئے مہیا کی گئی ہے تو زمین کا مالک ان چیزوں کا
مالک ہوگا ۔
بخلاف العسل .. الخ سے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی کی زمین میں شہد کی مکھیوں نے شہد جمع کیا ہو تو زمین کا مالک اس شہد کا مالک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شہد ایسی چیز ہے جو زمین کی پیدا وار اور حاصلات میں شمار ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شہد نہ تو ہر جگہ پیدا ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہر
A bird hatched chicks in a man's land; they will belong to the one who catches them. He said: If a bird hatches in a man's land, it belongs to the one who takes it. Likewise if it lays eggs, and likewise if a deer makes a lair. Because each of these is mubah (ownerless) and the hand that precedes to it gets it, and because it is game even if taken without a trick; and game belongs to the one who takes it. Likewise eggs, because they are the origin of game, and for this reason a pilgrim in ihram is liable for compensation for breaking or cooking them. And the landowner did not prepare his land for that; so it is like spreading a net for drying. And just as if game enters his house or scattered sugar or dirhams fall into his garments, it is not his unless he gathers or was prepared for it. Contrary to when bees make honey in his land, because it is considered as part of his produce, so he owns it as a follow-on to his land, like a tree growing in it or soil that accumulates in his land from flowing water.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning ownership of birds, their young, eggs, and game that appear on someone's land without the landowner's preparation. The core ruling from the matn states: if a bird hatches chicks in a man's land, they belong to the one who takes them (the catcher), not the landowner. The same applies if it lays eggs or if a deer makes a lair. The proof is twofold: (1) these items are mubah (ownerless) and therefore become the property of the first person to take possession; (2) they are considered game (sayd), and the hadith 'al-saydu li-man akhadhahu' (game belongs to the one who takes it) applies. Eggs are included because they are the origin of game, as evidenced by the fact that breaking them in ihram requires compensation. An exception occurs if the landowner prepared his land for this purpose (e.g., to attract birds), in which case he becomes the owner by virtue of his preparation. The text analogizes this to a net spread for drying vs. for hunting, or to a house where an animal enters—knowledge and intentional capture matter. A contrasting case is honey bees: honey is considered produce of the land (like trees and soil deposits), so it belongs to the landowner regardless of preparation. The commentary elaborates with examples to clarify the distinction.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game; wild animals or birds that are lawful to hunt and that can be owned by capture.
مباح (mubah): Ownerless; permissible to acquire by taking possession.
جزاء (jaza): Compensation or penalty; specifically here, the fine for breaking eggs while in ihram, similar to hunting.
إحراز (ihraz): Taking possession; the act of acquiring ownership of a mubah item by physically taking it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The landowner because it is on his land.
B) The first person to catch it.
C) The person who sees it first.
D) The government.

Key Takeaway
Ownerless game on unprepared land belongs to the first to capture it, not the landowner.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Definition and Etymology of Bay' al-Sarf
Definition and etymology of Sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Sarf and explain the two linguistic bases for its naming.

Core Idea
Sarf is a sale of prices for prices, named for the required hand-to-hand transfer or for the increase sought.

This lesson unpacks the opening of the chapter on Sarf (currency exchange) from Ashraf al-Hidayah. We first examine why this chapter is placed last among sales: because both countervalues are thaman (price), which is secondary in a sale contract. Then we learn the precise definition of Sarf from al-Quduri and the two etymological reasons for its name: one based on 'transfer' and the other on 'increase'. Understanding this foundation is essential before studying the detailed rulings of spot exchange of gold, silver, and currencies.

Guided Path
1
Understand the placement of the chapter
Note that Sarf is mentioned last among types of sales. The author explains that in a sale, the sold item is the origin (asl) and the price is an attribute (wasf); since the attribute depends on the origin, sales of commodities precede sales where both items are prices.
This is a structural clue about the hierarchy of sales in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Memorize the legal definition
Sarf is a sale where each of the two countervalues belongs to the category of prices (athman). Examples: gold for gold, silver for silver, gold for silver, and any combination of currencies that serve as thaman.
The definition excludes commodity-for-commodity or commodity-for-price sales.
3
Analyze the first linguistic reason (naql)
The word 'sarf' literally means to transfer or turn around. The contract requires physical hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) of the two items before separation, fitting the meaning of 'transfer'.
Quranic evidence: 'Thumma insarafu, sarafa Allahu qulubahum' (Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts).
4
Analyze the second linguistic reason (ziyada)
According to al-Khalil, 'sarf' also means increase. In a sarf contract, the benefit is the excess (e.g., exchanging a smaller gold coin for a larger one or for silver), not intrinsic use of the coins themselves. Similarly, supererogatory worship (nafl) is called 'sarf' because it increases reward.
This reason connects to the hadith: '…Allah does not accept from him either sarf (supererogatory) or 'adl (obligatory).'

Translation: This book is about Bay' al-Sarf.
Chapter of Sarf
Explanation: Bay' al-Sarf is a type of sale, and among the types of sales, Bay' al-Sarf is postponed because in Sarf both countervalues are thaman (price). In the contract of sale, thaman stands in place of the attribute (wasf), and the sold item stands in place of the origin (asl). And everyone knows that the origin is mentioned first and the attribute later. Therefore, Bay' al-Sarf is mentioned last among the types of sales. (Should be from Badr al-Din al-Mu'ayyidi?)
Definition of Bay' al-Sarf: He said: Sarf is a sale when each of its two countervalues is from the category of prices. It is named thus due to the need for transfer (naql) of its two substitutes from hand to hand. And 'sarf' literally means transfer and return. Or because only increase (ziyada) is sought from it, as its essence is not benefited from. And 'sarf' literally means increase, as al-Khalil said, and from this the supererogatory worship is called 'sarf'.
Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri states that Bay' al-Sarf is a sale in which both countervalues are from the category of prices. It has three forms: gold for gold, silver for silver, and one of them for the other.
Sahib al-Hidayah mentioned two reasons for naming this contract 'Sarf'. The first reason is that 'sarf' literally means to turn/transfer, as in the divine saying: 'Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts' (Thumma insarafu, sarafa Allahu qulubahum). Since both countervalues in this contract need to be transferred hand to hand, it is named Sarf. The second reason, as per al-Khalil al-Nahwi, is that 'sarf' literally means increase, and for this reason supererogatory worship is called 'sarf'. Thus, the Hashimi Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever attributes himself to other than his father, Allah does not accept from him either supererogatory (sarf) or obligatory ('adl) deeds.'
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah introduces the Book of Sarf (currency exchange). The author first explains why Sarf is placed last among sales: because in Sarf both items are considered thaman (price), which is secondary to the sold commodity (muthman) in the sale contract. Since the origin (asl) takes precedence over the attribute (wasf), and thaman is like an attribute, the chapter on Sarf is deferred. The author then gives the definition from al-Quduri: Sarf is a sale where both countervalues are from the category of prices (gold, silver, or currency). Three scenarios: gold for gold, silver for silver, or gold for silver (or vice versa). Two etymological reasons for the name 'Sarf' are cited from al-Hidayah: (1) 'Sarf' means transfer/return, because the two items must be exchanged on the spot (hand-to-hand). (2) 'Sarf' means increase, because the benefit of such exchange is only the excess (e.g., different amounts of same species), and supererogatory worship is also called 'sarf' as it increases reward. A hadith is quoted to illustrate this linguistic usage. The passage establishes the conceptual framework for the detailed rulings of Sarf that follow.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): A sale where both countervalues are from the category of prices (gold, silver, or currency), requiring immediate hand-to-hand exchange.
ثمن (thaman): Price; in Sarf, both items are considered thaman as they serve as mediums of exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for naming this contract 'Sarf'?
A) Because it involves a sale of commodities
B) Because it requires hand-to-hand transfer of the countervalues
C) Because it is prohibited in Islam
D) Because it is a sale of foodstuffs

Key Takeaway
Bay' al-Sarf is a sale of prices for prices, named for the required hand-to-hand transfer or for the increase sought, and its definition determines the strict conditions for validity.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sarf: Definition and Ruling on Exchange of Gold and Silver
Defines Sarf and states ruling with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sarf linguistically and technically, state the two conditions for a valid sale of gold for gold or silver for silver, and derive the ruling from the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Gold for gold must be equal in weight and hand-to-hand; any excess or delay is riba.

This lesson introduces a special type of sale known as Sarf (currency exchange), where both countervalues are prices. You will learn its linguistic and technical meanings, why it is placed last among sales, and the strict rules governing the exchange of gold and silver. The core ruling is that gold for gold (or silver for silver) is valid only if equal in weight and delivered hand-to-hand in the same session, regardless of quality. The Prophet's hadith on riba provides the proof, emphasizing that any excess is riba.

Guided Path
1
Define Sarf linguistically and technically
Identify the two linguistic meanings (transfer and increase) and how they relate to the contract. Then state the technical definition: a sale where both countervalues are from the genus of prices.
The linguistic meaning of 'increase' connects to the purpose of Sarf: obtaining profit from exchange, not from the intrinsic use of gold/silver.
2
Explain why the book of Sarf is placed last
Understand the author's reasoning: the price (thaman) is subordinate to the sold item, and in Sarf both items are prices, so it is the most restricted and placed after other sales.
This reflects the principle that attribute follows essence.
3
State the two conditions for a valid same-species Sarf
From the hadith, extract the conditions: equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery in the same session. Note that quality differences do not permit weight inequality.
The hadith explicitly says 'equal for equal, weight for weight, hand to hand'.
4
Identify the proof and its legal implication
Locate the two hadith cited: the famous riba hadith listing six commodities and the hadith 'its good and bad are equal'. Explain how the imperative phrasing generates the conditions of obligation (wajib) and the consequence of excess being riba.
The hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning by many Hanafis, giving it strong evidentiary weight.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
Test the ruling: e.g., 10g of pure gold for 12g of impure gold is invalid because weight not equal; 10g gold for 10g gold with deferred delivery is invalid because not hand-to-hand.
Even if the quality differs, weight must match exactly.

اس حدیث میں لفظ صرف عبادت نافلہ کیلئے استعمال کیا گیا ہے اور عبادت نافلہ بھی فرائض سے زائد ایک چیز ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ صرف کے معنی زیادتی کے ہیں اور عقد صرف سے مطلوب بھی زیادتی ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ سونا اور چاندی دونوں ایسی چیزیں ہیں جن کی ذات سے کوئی نفع نہیں اٹھایا جاتا ہے۔ اسکے بر خلاف اناج، کپڑا اور گدھا وغیرہ کہ ان کی ذات سے نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ اناج سے پیٹ بھرتا ہے اور کپڑے سے ستر کا کام لیا جاتا ہے اور گدھا سواری کے کام میں آتا ہے۔ پس جب سونے اور چاندی کی ذات غیر مشتقع بہ ہیں تو ان کی تجارت سے مقصور زیادتی کو طلب کرنا ہوگا۔ بایں طور کہ کھرے کے بدلے میں کھوٹا دےدے یا بغیر ڈھلے ہوئے کے بدلے میں ڈھلا ہوالے لے ۔ اسلئے کہ اگر ان کی تجارت سے زیادتی بھی مطلوب نہ ہو تو عقد صرف فائدہ سے خالی ہوگا۔ حالانکہ عقد کرنے سے عاقدین کا مقصود کوئی نہ کوئی فائدہ ضرور ہوتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ عقد صرف سے زیادتی مطلوب ہوتی ہے اور صرف کے لغوی معنی بھی چونکہ زیادتی کے ہیں۔ اسلئے اس عقد کا نام صرف رکھا گیا ہے۔
چاندی کی چاندی کے بدلے سونے کی سونے کے بدلے برابر سرا بر بیع جائز ہے
قال فإن باع فضة بفضة او ذهباً بذهب لا يجوز الامثلاً بمثل وان اختلفت فى الجودة والصياغة لقوله عليه السلام الذهب بالذهب مثلاً بمثل وزنا بوزن يدا بيد والفضل ربوا (الحديث وقال عليه السلام جيدها ورديها سواء وقد ذكرناه في البيوع
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے چاندی کو چاندی کے عوض یا سونے کو سونے کے عوض بیچا تو جائز نہیں ہے مگر برابر، برابر۔ اگر چہ کھرے ہونے اور ڈھلائی میں مختلف ہو کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سونا سونے کے عوض برابر برابر وز نابوزن ہاتھ درہاتھ اور زیادتی سود ہے۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان مالوں کا کھرا اور کھوٹا یکساں ہے اور ہم اس کو کتاب البیوع میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص چاندی ، چاندی کے عوض یا سونا سونے کے عوض فروخت کرے تو یہ عقد اس وقت جائز ہوگا جبکہ وزن کے اعتبار سے دونوں عوض برابر ہوں۔ اگر چہ جودت یا صیافت میں دونوں عوضوں کے درمیان فرق ہو۔ بایں طور کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک عوض عمدہ ڈھلا ہوا ہو اور دوسرا اس کے مقابلہ میں اتنا عمدہ ڈھلا ہوا نہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ اگر دونوں عوض جودت یا صیاغت میں مختلف وں تب بھی عقد جائز ہونے کیلئے دونوں عوضوں میں برابری ضروری ہے صاحب ہدایہ دلیل میں دو حدیثیں پیش فرما رہے ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ بادی عالم نے چھ چیزوں سونا چاندی گندم جو چھوہارے نمک کو کر کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے مثلاً بمثل وزناً بوزن وكيلاً بكيل يداً بيد والفضل ربو یعنی دو باتیں ضروری فرمائیں۔ ایک یہ کہ موزونات میں وزن کے ذریعہ اور مکیلات میں کیل کے ذریعہ برابری ہو۔ دوم یہ کہ مجلس عقد میں عوضین پر قبضہ ہو جائے ۔ اور اگر وزن یا کیل سے برابری نہ کی گئی یا مجلس میں قبضہ نہ کیا گیا تو یہ رہا اور حرام ہو گا۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ اموال ربویہ کی بیچ میں عوضین
This is the Book of Sarf (Currency Exchange). Translation: This book is about the sale of Sarf. Explanation: Sarf is a type of sale. It has been postponed among the types of sales because in Sarf both countervalues are price. In a sale contract, the price (thaman) stands in place of the attribute (sifah), and the sold item (mabi') stands in place of the original (asl). Everyone knows that the original is mentioned first and the attribute later. Therefore, Sarf is mentioned last among the types of sales. (From Badr al-Din al-Ayni). Definition of Sarf: He said: Sarf is a sale when each of its two countervalues is of the genus of prices (athman). It is named due to the need for transfer (naql) of its two countervalues from hand to hand. Linguistically, Sarf means transfer and return. Or because only increase (ziyada) is sought from it, as its essence does not give benefit. Linguistically, Sarf means increase. Thus said al-Khalil, and from it the supererogatory act of worship is called Sarf. Translation: Sarf is a sale when each of its two countervalues is of the genus of price. This contract is named Sarf because both countervalues require hand-to-hand transfer. Sarf linguistically means to transfer and turn back. Or because only increase is sought from this contract, since its essence does not derive benefit. Linguistically, Sarf means increase, as al-Khalil al-Nahwi said, and from this supererogatory worship is called Sarf. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that Bai' al-Sarf is a sale where both countervalues are of the genus of price. It has three forms: gold for gold, silver for silver, or one of them for the other. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned two reasons for naming this contract Sarf. First, Sarf linguistically means to turn back and transfer, as in the verse 'Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts.' Since both countervalues must be transferred hand-to-hand, it is called Sarf. Second, according to al-Khalil, Sarf means increase. Thus supererogatory worship is called Sarf. The Prophet said: 'Whoever attributes himself to other than his father, Allah will not accept from him Sarf (supererogatory) nor 'Adl (obligatory).' In this hadith, the word Sarf is used for supererogatory worship, which is something additional to obligations. So it became clear that Sarf means increase, and in the contract of Sarf, increase is sought because gold and silver are not beneficial in themselves, unlike grain, cloth, donkey etc., from which benefit is derived. Since gold and silver are not inherently beneficial, trade in them seeks increase by giving impure for pure or unminted for minted. If increase were not sought, the contract would be devoid of benefit. So it is established that increase is sought in Sarf, and since the linguistic meaning of Sarf is also increase, therefore this contract is named Sarf. The sale of silver for silver or gold for gold is permissible only equal for equal. He said: If someone sells silver for silver or gold for gold, it is not permissible except equal for equal, even if they differ in purity and workmanship, because the Prophet said: 'Gold for gold, equal for equal, weight for weight, hand to hand; and excess is riba.' And the Prophet said: 'Its good and bad are equal.' And we mentioned it in the Book of Sales. Translation: If someone sells silver for silver or gold for gold, it is not permissible except equal for equal, even if they differ in purity and casting, because the Prophet said: Gold for gold, equal for equal, weight for weight, hand to hand; and excess is riba. And the Prophet said: The good and bad of these commodities are equal. And we mentioned it in the Book of Sales. Explanation: The issue is that if a person sells silver for silver or gold for gold, the contract is valid only if both countervalues are equal in weight, even if they differ in purity (joodat) or craftsmanship (siyaghat). The author of al-Hidayah presents two hadith as proof. One: The Prophet specified six items: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, and salt, saying: 'Equal for equal, weight for weight, measure for measure, hand to hand; and excess is riba.' He made two conditions: equality by weight for weight-based items and by measure for measure-based items, and possession in the assembly. If equality in weight or measure is not observed, or possession is not taken in the assembly, it is riba and forbidden. From this hadith it is established that in dealing with ribawi commodities, the countervalues must be equal and hand-to-hand.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Sarf (Currency Exchange). It begins by defining Sarf technically as a sale where both countervalues are from the genus of prices (gold, silver, or currency). The author explains why this chapter is placed last among types of sales: because the price is subordinate to the sold item, and Sarf involves two prices, so it is the most restricted form. The linguistic derivation is explored: Sarf can mean 'transfer' (hand-to-hand delivery) or 'increase' (since the intrinsic benefit of gold/silver is not sought, only gain in exchange). The passage then states the core ruling: selling gold for gold or silver for silver is only permissible if equal in weight and hand-to-hand, regardless of quality or craftsmanship. This is proven by two hadith: the famous riba hadith listing the six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) and the hadith that 'its good and bad are equal.' The commentary by Sahib al-Hidayah emphasizes that any excess in weight or delay in delivery constitutes riba, which is haram. The author also clarifies that the purpose of Sarf is to obtain profit through exchange, not use of the items themselves. The three scenarios of Sarf (gold for gold, silver for silver, gold for silver) are hinted at, but the ruling here specifically treats same-species exchanges where equality is mandatory.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Technically: a sale where both countervalues are of the genus of prices (gold, silver, or currency). Often refers to exchange of gold/silver or currency exchange.
ربا (riba): Excess in exchange of ribawi commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) without hand-to-hand delivery.
ثمن (thaman): Price; in Sarf, both countervalues are considered thaman (price) because they are currency or currency-like.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a sale of silver for silver invalid?
A) The silver is of different purity levels.
B) The weight of the silver is not equal.
C) The silver is in coin form vs. bar form.
D) The buyer and seller are of different religions.

Key Takeaway
In Sarf, exchanging gold for gold or silver for silver requires equality in weight and immediate hand-to-hand delivery; any deviation constitutes riba.
